1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Task: Kubernetes API Server Architecture and Extension Guide

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0 (mirror of kubernetes/kubernetes) (stripped snapshot)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce a subsystem architecture and extension guide for the apiserver library with request-path flow and extension tradeoffs.

## Scope

Focus on the Kubernetes apiserver library subsystem.
Your document must explain component responsibilities, end-to-end flow, and extension or operational tradeoffs.

## Content Expectations

Address all of the following in your own structure:
- subsystem purpose, boundaries, and upstream/downstream dependencies
- key components and how responsibilities are split
- end-to-end control/request flow with concrete repository evidence
- failure modes, limits, and design tradeoffs
- extension points, customization hooks, and associated risks
- a concise map of the most important files/directories used in your analysis

## Quality Bar

- Cite concrete file paths from the repository.
- Explain behavior and interactions, not just API signatures.
- Include at least one section on operational implications (performance, reliability, or maintainability).
- Do not fabricate classes, functions, or files.

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not output `doc.go`.
- Do not provide shallow bullet dumps without system flow explanation.
- Do not rely on external docs not present in the workspace.

{"content":"1: # apiserver Architecture\n2: \n3: ## 1. Server Composition\n4: \n5: The `kube-apiserver` binary is not one server, but a **server chain** of three distinct\n6: `GenericAPIServer` instances: the core Kubernetes API, API extensions (CRDs), and the aggregation\n7: layer.\n8: \n9: This composition is managed by a layered configuration system, starting with command-line\n10: flags parsed by `options` structs (e.g., `RecommendedOptions` in `pkg/server/options`), which\n11: populate a `Config` object that is then used to instantiate the `GenericAPIServer`\n12: instances. The construction of this delegation chain can be found in the `CreateServerChain`\n13: function in `cmd/kube-apiserver/app/server.go`.\n14: \n15: ```mermaid\n16: graph TD\n17:     subgraph Incoming Request\n18:         direction LR\n19:         A[User/Client] --> B{/apis/apps/v1/deployments};\n20:     end\n21: \n22:     subgraph kube-apiserver process\n23:         direction LR\n24:         B --> C[Aggregator Server];\n25:         C -- Not an APIService --> D[Kube API Server];\n26:         D -- Handles Request --> E[REST Storage];\n27:         C -- Is an APIService --> F[Proxy to Extension API Server];\n28:         D -- Not a Core API --> G[API Extensions Server];\n29:         G -- Handles CRD --> E;\n30:     end\n31: ```\n32: \n33: 1.  **Aggregator Server (`kube-aggregator`):**\n34:     *   **Purpose:** Handles the `apiregistration.k8s.io` API and acts as a reverse proxy for\n35:         extension API servers. Server Composition\\n4: \\n5: The `kube-apiserver` binary is not one server, but a **server chain** of three distinct\\n6: `GenericAPIServer` instances: the core Kubernetes API, API extensions (CRDs), and the aggregation\\n7: layer.\\n8: \\n9: This composition is managed by a layered configuration system, starting with command-line\\n10: flags parsed by `options` structs (e.g., `RecommendedOptions` in `pkg/server/options`), which\\n11: populate a `Config` object that is then used to instantiate the `GenericAPIServer`\\n12: instances. The construction of this delegation chain can be found in the `CreateServerChain`\\n13: function in `cmd/kube-apiserver/app/server.go`.\\n14: \\n15: ```mermaid\\n16: graph TD\\n17:     subgraph Incoming Request\\n18:         direction LR\\n19:         A[User/Client] --> B{/apis/apps/v1/deployments};\\n20:     end\\n21: \\n22:     subgraph kube-apiserver process\\n23:         direction LR\\n24:         B --> C[Aggregator Server];\\n25:         C -- Not an APIService --> D[Kube API Server];\\n26:         D -- Handles Request --> E[REST Storage];\\n27:         C -- Is an APIService --> F[Proxy to Extension API Server];\\n28:         D -- Not a Core API --> G[API Extensions Server];\\n29:         G -- Handles CRD --> E;\\n30:     end\\n31: ```\\n32: \\n33: 1.  **Aggregator Server (`kube-aggregator`):**\\n34:     *   **Purpose:** Handles the `apiregistration.k8s.io` API and acts as a reverse proxy for\\n35:         extension API servers. This functionality was designed to allow third-party APIs to be\\n36:         \\\"aggregated\\\" into the main Kubernetes API server seamlessly.\\n37:     *   **Mechanism:** It watches `APIService` objects. When a request arrives (e.g., for\\n38:         `/apis/mycompany.com/v1/myresources`), it checks if an `APIService` has \\\"claimed\\\"\\n39:         that path. If so, it uses a `ServiceResolver` to find the IP of the backing\\n40:         `Service` and proxies the request.\\n41:     *   **Use Case:** This pattern is for programmatic, high-control extensions that require\\n42:         custom business logic (e.g., non-CRUD subresources like `/logs`) or alternative\\n43:         storage backends.\\n44:     *   **Delegation:** If no `APIService` matches, it delegates the request to the next\\n45:         server in the chain.\\n46: \\n47: 2.  **Kube API Server (Core):**\\n48:     *   **Purpose:** Serves all the built-in Kubernetes APIs (`core/v1`, `apps/v1`, etc.).\\n49:     *   **Mechanism:** This is the main server, configured with all the core REST storage\\n50:         strategies.\\n51:     *   **Delegation:** If a request is for a path that is not a core API (e.g., for a CRD),\\n52:         it delegates the request to the next server in the chain.\\n53: \\n54: 3.  **API Extensions Server (`apiextensions-apiserver`):**\\n55:     *   **Purpose:** Handles the `apiextensions.k8s.io` API, which manages\\n56:         `CustomResourceDefinition` objects (CRDs). The evolution of CRDs from a simple extension\\n57:         mechanism to a feature-rich system with validation, versioning, and defaulting is\\n58:         documented in a series of KEPs, starting with the graduation to GA in Kubernetes v1.16.\\n59:     *   **Mechanism:** When a CRD is created, this server dynamically creates and installs a\\n60:         new REST storage handler for the new resource, making it immediately available.\\n61:     *   **Use Case:** CRDs are the most common extension pattern, offering a declarative,\\n62:         schema-based way to define new resource types that are stored in etcd and require no\\n63:         custom API server code.\\n64:     *   **Delegation:** It is the end of the chain. If it cannot handle a request, a `404 Not\\n65:         Found` is returned.\\n66: \\n67: ## 2. Handler Chain\\n68: \\n69: Every request flows through a standard chain of HTTP handlers (filters). The request body\\n70: is not deserialized until it has passed authentication and authorization. The default handler\\n71: chain is constructed by the `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` function in\\n72: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go`.\\n73: \\n74: ```mermaid\\n75: sequenceDiagram\\n76:     participant Client\\n77:     participant Handler Chain\\n78:     participant Authentication\\n79:     participant Authorization\\n80:     participant Priority and Fairness\\n81:     participant Admission Control\\n82:     participant REST Endpoint\\n83: \\n84:     Client->>Handler Chain: Request\\n85:     Handler Chain->>Authentication: Authenticate\\n86:     Authentication-->>Handler Chain: User Info\\n87:     Handler Chain->>Authorization: Authorize\\n88:     Authorization-->>Handler Chain: Allowed/Denied\\n89:     Handler Chain->>Priority and Fairness: Classify & Queue\\n90:     Priority and Fairness-->>Handler Chain: Proceed\\n91:     Handler Chain->>Admission Control: Mutate & Validate\\n92:     Admission Control-->>Handler Chain: Object OK\\n93:     Handler Chain->>REST Endpoint: Handle\\n94:     REST Endpoint-->>Handler Chain: Response\\n95:     Handler Chain-->>Client: Response\\n96: ```\\n97: \\n98: The handler chain consists of the following stages:\\n99: \\n100: 1.  **Authentication (`pkg/authentication`):** This filter identifies the user. The system is\\n101:     pluggable and composed of multiple authenticators (e.g., client certs, bearer tokens, OIDC).\\n102:     The identity of the user is determined by the first authenticator in the chain that successfully\\n103:     identifies the user.\\n104: 2.  **Authorization (`pkg/authorization`):** This filter checks if the user is permitted to\\n105:     perform the action. This system is also pluggable and composed of multiple authorizers\\n106:     (e.g., RBAC, Node, Webhook). Each authorizer may respond with either allow, deny, or no opinion.\\n107:     If the response is no opinion, the request is passed to the next authorizer in the chain.\\n108: 3.  **Priority and Fairness (`pkg/util/flowcontrol`):** This subsystem manages request\\n109:     concurrency, classifying requests into `FlowSchema`s and `PriorityLevel`s to prevent\\n110:     overload. This feature was introduced to prevent high traffic from overwhelming the API\\n111:     server and to ensure that critical cluster operations are not starved.\\n112: 4.  **Admission Control (`pkg/admission`):** This is the primary mechanism for policy\\n113:     enforcement. It is only at this stage that the request body is deserialized into an\\n114:     object. It is a chain of plugins that can mutate or validate an object. The built-in Pod\\n115:     Security admission controller is a key example of this, enforcing Pod Security Standards\\n116:     at the namespace level.\\n117: 5.  **REST Endpoint Handling (`pkg/endpoints`):** The request is finally dispatched to the\\n118:     appropriate REST handler, which is installed by the `APIInstaller`.\\n119: \\n120: ## 3. API Group Registration\\n121: \\n122: The high-level steps for introducing an API are:\\n123: \\n124: 1.  **Define Types:** Create or modify the Go structs in the `types.go` file for the API group.\\n125: 2.  **Generate Code:** Use the code generators provided by the Kubernetes project to create the required\\n126:     boilerplate methods for deep-copy, conversion, and defaulting.\\n127: 3.  **Implement the `Strategy`:** Write the custom business logic and validation for the\\n128:     resource in its `Strategy` object.\\n129: 4.  **Register and Install:** Create the `APIGroupInfo` struct, bundling the `Scheme` and the\\n130:     `Strategy`-configured storage, and pass it to the `GenericAPIServer`'s `InstallAPIGroup`\\n131:     method.\\n132: \\n133: ### The API Group Registry\\n134: \\n135: The `runtime.Scheme` acts as a central registry for an API group's type information. A single\\n136: `Scheme` object is created for each API group and is responsible for the following key\\n137: capabilities:\\n138: \\n139: *   **Type Registration and Mapping:** The `Scheme`'s primary role is to map a GroupVersionKind\\n140:     (GVK) to its corresponding Go type and back. This process also relies on the `deepcopy-gen`\\n141:     tool to create `DeepCopy()` methods for each type, which is critical for ensuring that\\n142:     objects returned from caches are never modified directly.\\n143: \\n144: *   **API Conversion:** The `Scheme` stores the conversion functions that translate objects\\n145:     between different API versions. These functions are typically generated by the\\n146:     `conversion-gen` tool and enable the **hub-and-spoke** model.\\n147: \\n148: *   **Defaulting:** The `Scheme` registers defaulting functions that populate optional fields in\\n149:     an object. These are usually generated by the `defaulter-gen` tool.\\n150: \\n151: *   **Declarative Validation:** The `Scheme` can store and execute code-generated validation\\n152:     functions, providing a baseline level of validation. This is distinct from the primary,\\n153:     handwritten business logic validation, which is handled by the `Strategy` object.\\n154: \\n155: ### The `APIGroupInfo` Struct and `Strategy` Object\\n156: \\n157: With a populated `Scheme`, the API group is registered with the `GenericAPIServer` by bundling\\n158: the `Scheme` with the storage backend and versioning information into an `APIGroupInfo` struct.\\n159: \\n160: ```mermaid\\n161: graph TD\\n162:     subgraph Server Configuration\\n163:         A[APIGroupInfo for apps v1];\\n164:         A --> B{Scheme: Knows Deployment v1};\\n165:         A --> C{Storage: deployments RESTStorage};\\n166:         A --> D{Version Priority: v1, v1beta1};\\n167:     end\\n168: \\n169:     subgraph RESTStorage Implementation\\n170:         C --> E[genericregistry.Store];\\n171:         E --> F[etcd client];\\n172:         E --> G[Deployment Strategy];\\n173:     end\\n174: \\n175:     subgraph Server Runtime\\n176:         H[GenericAPIServer] -- InstallAPIGroup --> I[APIInstaller];\\n177:         I -- Uses --> A;\\n178:         I --> J{Register /apis/apps/v1/deployments};\\n179:         J --> K[HTTP Handler];\\n180:         K -- On Request --> C;\\n181:     end\\n182: ```\\n183: \\n184: The registration process follows these steps:\\n185: \\n186: 1.  **`APIGroupInfo` Construction:** For each API group, an `APIGroupInfo` struct is created,\\n187:     which contains the populated `Scheme`, a map of resources to their storage\\n188:     implementations, and an ordered list of **Version Priority**.\\n189: \\n190: 2.  **REST Storage Instantiation:** For each resource, a `genericregistry.Store` is created. It\\n191:     is configured with a resource-specific `Strategy` object that contains the core business\\n192:     logic (e.g., handwritten validation).\\n193: \\n194: 3.  **API Group Installation:** The `GenericAPIServer`'s `InstallAPIGroup` method takes the\\n195:     `APIGroupInfo` and uses an `APIInstaller` to expose the resources as HTTP endpoints.\\n196: \\n197: ## 4. Watch Cache\\n198: \\n199: To handle the high volume of watch requests from controllers without overwhelming etcd, the\\n200: apiserver uses a **watch cache**. The implementation can be found in\\n201: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/`.\\n202: \\n203: *   **Initialization:** The cacher first performs a `LIST` to get the current state of all\\n204:     objects and a `ResourceVersion` for that point-in-time. It then starts a `WATCH` from\\n205:     that version to ensure a consistent stream of events.\\n206: *   **Serving from Cache:** Most list and watch requests are served from this in-memory cache, which\\n207:     dramatically reduces the load on etcd. Consistent reads are also served from the\\n208:     cache. This is achieved by first fetching the revision number of the latest write from\\n209:     etcd. The server then ensures the cache is at least that recent\u2014waiting for it to\\n210:     refresh if necessary\u2014before serving the request.\\n211: *   **Fallback to Storage:** If a client request cannot be served from the\\n212:     cache's buffer, the request \\\"falls through\\\" to the underlying etcd storage.\\n213: *   **Bookmarks:** The cacher uses bookmark events to track the latest `ResourceVersion` for\\n214:     unchanged objects. This prevents the cache's `ResourceVersion` from becoming too old,\\n215:     which avoids the need for expensive relist operations from etcd when the objects have\\n216:     not been modified.\\n217: \\n218: ## 5. Conflict Resolution\\n219: \\n220: *   **Optimistic Concurrency via `resourceVersion`:** Clients are expected to perform updates using a\\n221:     read-modify-write workflow. The apiserver uses the `resourceVersion` field of every\\n222:     object to enforce optimistic concurrency. This `resourceVersion` is not an arbitrary number;\\n223:     it maps directly to etcd's globally consistent `mod_revision`. When a client submits an\\n224:     update (`PUT` or `PATCH`), it must provide the `resourceVersion` of the object it based its\\n225:     modifications on. If the `resourceVersion` on the server does not match the current\\n226:     `mod_revision` in etcd, the server rejects the request with a `409 Conflict` error. This\\n227:     forces the client to re-read the object, resolve the conflict, and resubmit with the new\\n228:     `resourceVersion`.\\n229: *   **Server-Side Apply:** A declarative, \\\"intent-based\\\" patch. The server maintains a\\n230:     `managedFields` section in the object's metadata to track which \\\"manager\\\" (e.g., a\\n231:     controller) owns each field. This allows multiple actors to manage different parts of the\\n232:     same object without overwriting each other's changes.\\n233: \\n234: ## 6. Discovery and OpenAPI\\n235: \\n236: Apiservers serve the `/apis` discovery endpoints and the `/openapi/v2` and `/openapi/v3`\\n237: specifications. The generation of the OpenAPI specification is a multi-stage process.\\n238: \\n239: *   **`openapi-gen`**: This tool reflects on Go structs, reads godoc comments, and looks at\\n240:     validation struct tags to generate a map of all API definitions.\\n241: *   **`zz_generated.openapi.go`**: The output is a large Go file containing a\\n242:     `GetOpenAPIDefinitions` function.\\n243: *   **Runtime**: The `GenericAPIServer` calls this generated function to build the final OpenAPI\\n244:     JSON spec that it serves to clients.\\n245: \\n246: ## 7. Security & Observability\\n247: \\n248: *   **Audit (`pkg/audit`):** The apiserver has a policy-driven event logging pipeline. The audit\\n249:     policy controls what is logged and at which stage of a request.\\n250: *   **Security:**\\n251:     *   **mTLS:** The primary authentication mechanism for system components.\\n252:     *   **Service Account Token Issuance:** The `kube-apiserver` acts as an OIDC provider,\\n253:         issuing and validating JWTs for `ServiceAccount`s.\\n254: \\n255: ## 8. Streaming Protocols\\n256: \\n257: *   **Websockets:** The apiserver uses websockets to upgrade HTTP\\n258:     connections for interactive, streaming protocols like `exec`, `attach`, and\\n259:     `port-forward`. The `UpgradeAwareProxyHandler` manages this process.\\n260: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0@8c9c67c000104450cfc5a5f48053a9a84b73cf93/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/ARCHITECTURE.md\"}",

This functionality was designed to allow third-party APIs to be\n36:         \"aggregated\" into the main Kubernetes API server seamlessly.\n37:     *   **Mechanism:** It watches `APIService` objects. When a request arrives (e.g., for\n38:         `/apis/mycompany.com/v1/myresources`), it checks if an `APIService` has \"claimed\"\n39:         that path. If so, it uses a `ServiceResolver` to find the IP of the backing\n40:         `Service` and proxies the request.\n41:     *   **Use Case:** This pattern is for programmatic, high-control extensions that require\n42:         custom business logic (e.g., non-CRUD subresources like `/logs`) or alternative\n43:         storage backends.\n44:     *   **Delegation:** If no `APIService` matches, it delegates the request to the next\n45:         server in the chain.\n46: \n47: 2.  **Kube API Server (Core):**\n48:     *   **Purpose:** Serves all the built-in Kubernetes APIs (`core/v1`, `apps/v1`, etc.).\n49:     *   **Mechanism:** This is the main server, configured with all the core REST storage\n50:         strategies.\n51:     *   **Delegation:** If a request is for a path that is not a core API (e.g., for a CRD),\n52:         it delegates the request to the next server in the chain.\n53: \n54: 3.  **API Extensions Server (`apiextensions-apiserver`):**\n55:     *   **Purpose:** Handles the `apiextensions.k8s.io` API, which manages\n56:         `CustomResourceDefinition` objects (CRDs). The evolution of CRDs from a simple extension\n57:         mechanism to a feature-rich system with validation, versioning, and defaulting is\n58:         documented in a series of KEPs, starting with the graduation to GA in Kubernetes v1.16.\n59:     *   **Mechanism:** When a CRD is created, this server dynamically creates and installs a\n60:         new REST storage handler for the new resource, making it immediately available.\n61:     *   **Use Case:** CRDs are the most common extension pattern, offering a declarative,\n62:         schema-based way to define new resource types that are stored in etcd and require no\n63:         custom API server code.\n64:     *   **Delegation:** It is the end of the chain. If it cannot handle a request, a `404 Not\n65:         Found` is returned.\n66: \n67: ## 2. Handler Chain\n68: \n69: Every request flows through a standard chain of HTTP handlers (filters). The request body\n70: is not deserialized until it has passed authentication and authorization. The default handler\n71: chain is constructed by the `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` function in\n72: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go`.\n73: \n74: ```mermaid\n75: sequenceDiagram\n76:     participant Client\n77:     participant Handler Chain\n78:     participant Authentication\n79:     participant Authorization\n80:     participant Priority and Fairness\n81:     participant Admission Control\n82:     participant REST Endpoint\n83: \n84:     Client->>Handler Chain: Request\n85:     Handler Chain->>Authentication: Authenticate\n86:     Authentication-->>Handler Chain: User Info\n87:     Handler Chain->>Authorization: Authorize\n88:     Authorization-->>Handler Chain: Allowed/Denied\n89:     Handler Chain->>Priority and Fairness: Classify & Queue\n90:     Priority and Fairness-->>Handler Chain: Proceed\n91:     Handler Chain->>Admission Control: Mutate & Validate\n92:     Admission Control-->>Handler Chain: Object OK\n93:     Handler Chain->>REST Endpoint: Handle\n94:     REST Endpoint-->>Handler Chain: Response\n95:     Handler Chain-->>Client: Response\n96: ```\n97: \n98: The handler chain consists of the following stages:\n99: \n100: 1.  **Authentication (`pkg/authentication`):** This filter identifies the user. The system is\n101:     pluggable and composed of multiple authenticators (e.g., client certs, bearer tokens, OIDC).\n102:     The identity of the user is determined by the first authenticator in the chain that successfully\n103:     identifies the user.\n104: 2.  **Authorization (`pkg/authorization`):** This filter checks if the user is permitted to\n105:     perform the action. This system is also pluggable and composed of multiple authorizers\n106:     (e.g., RBAC, Node, Webhook). Each authorizer may respond with either allow, deny, or no opinion.\n107:     If the response is no opinion, the request is passed to the next authorizer in the chain.\n108: 3.  **Priority and Fairness (`pkg/util/flowcontrol`):** This subsystem manages request\n109:     concurrency, classifying requests into `FlowSchema`s and `PriorityLevel`s to prevent\n110:     overload. This feature was introduced to prevent high traffic from overwhelming the API\n111:     server and to ensure that critical cluster operations are not starved.\n112: 4.  **Admission Control (`pkg/admission`):** This is the primary mechanism for policy\n113:     enforcement. It is only at this stage that the request body is deserialized into an\n114:     object. It is a chain of plugins that can mutate or validate an object. The built-in Pod\n115:     Security admission controller is a key example of this, enforcing Pod Security Standards\n116:     at the namespace level.\n117: 5.  **REST Endpoint Handling (`pkg/endpoints`):** The request is finally dispatched to the\n118:     appropriate REST handler, which is installed by the `APIInstaller`.\n119: \n120: ## 3. API Group Registration\n121: \n122: The high-level steps for introducing an API are:\n123: \n124: 1.  **Define Types:** Create or modify the Go structs in the `types.go` file for the API group.\n125: 2.  **Generate Code:** Use the code generators provided by the Kubernetes project to create the required\n126:     boilerplate methods for deep-copy, conversion, and defaulting.\n127: 3.  **Implement the `Strategy`:** Write the custom business logic and validation for the\n128:     resource in its `Strategy` object.\n129: 4.  **Register and Install:** Create the `APIGroupInfo` struct, bundling the `Scheme` and the\n130:     `Strategy`-configured storage, and pass it to the `GenericAPIServer`'s `InstallAPIGroup`\n131:     method.\n132: \n133: ### The API Group Registry\n134: \n135: The `runtime.Scheme` acts as a central registry for an API group's type information. A single\n136: `Scheme` object is created for each API group and is responsible for the following key\n137: capabilities:\n138: \n139: *   **Type Registration and Mapping:** The `Scheme`'s primary role is to map a GroupVersionKind\n140:     (GVK) to its corresponding Go type and back. This process also relies on the `deepcopy-gen`\n141:     tool to create `DeepCopy()` methods for each type, which is critical for ensuring that\n142:     objects returned from caches are never modified directly.\n143: \n144: *   **API Conversion:** The `Scheme` stores the conversion functions that translate objects\n145:     between different API versions. These functions are typically generated by the\n146:     `conversion-gen` tool and enable the **hub-and-spoke** model.\n147: \n148: *   **Defaulting:** The `Scheme` registers defaulting functions that populate optional fields in\n149:     an object. These are usually generated by the `defaulter-gen` tool.\n150: \n151: *   **Declarative Validation:** The `Scheme` can store and execute code-generated validation\n152:     functions, providing a baseline level of validation. This is distinct from the primary,\n153:     handwritten business logic validation, which is handled by the `Strategy` object.\n154: \n155: ### The `APIGroupInfo` Struct and `Strategy` Object\n156: \n157: With a populated `Scheme`, the API group is registered with the `GenericAPIServer` by bundling\n158: the `Scheme` with the storage backend and versioning information into an `APIGroupInfo` struct.\n159: \n160: ```mermaid\n161: graph TD\n162:     subgraph Server Configuration\n163:         A[APIGroupInfo for apps v1];\n164:         A --> B{Scheme: Knows Deployment v1};\n165:         A --> C{Storage: deployments RESTStorage};\n166:         A --> D{Version Priority: v1, v1beta1};\n167:     end\n168: \n169:     subgraph RESTStorage Implementation\n170:         C --> E[genericregistry.Store];\n171:         E --> F[etcd client];\n172:         E --> G[Deployment Strategy];\n173:     end\n174: \n175:     subgraph Server Runtime\n176:         H[GenericAPIServer] -- InstallAPIGroup --> I[APIInstaller];\n177:         I -- Uses --> A;\n178:         I --> J{Register /apis/apps/v1/deployments};\n179:         J --> K[HTTP Handler];\n180:         K -- On Request --> C;\n181:     end\n182: ```\n183: \n184: The registration process follows these steps:\n185: \n186: 1.  **`APIGroupInfo` Construction:** For each API group, an `APIGroupInfo` struct is created,\n187:     which contains the populated `Scheme`, a map of resources to their storage\n188:     implementations, and an ordered list of **Version Priority**.\n189: \n190: 2.  **REST Storage Instantiation:** For each resource, a `genericregistry.Store` is created. It\n191:     is configured with a resource-specific `Strategy` object that contains the core business\n192:     logic (e.g., handwritten validation).\n193: \n194: 3.  **API Group Installation:** The `GenericAPIServer`'s `InstallAPIGroup` method takes the\n195:     `APIGroupInfo` and uses an `APIInstaller` to expose the resources as HTTP endpoints.\n196: \n197: ## 4. Watch Cache\n198: \n199: To handle the high volume of watch requests from controllers without overwhelming etcd, the\n200: apiserver uses a **watch cache**. The implementation can be found in\n201: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/`.\n202: \n203: *   **Initialization:** The cacher first performs a `LIST` to get the current state of all\n204:     objects and a `ResourceVersion` for that point-in-time. It then starts a `WATCH` from\n205:     that version to ensure a consistent stream of events.\n206: *   **Serving from Cache:** Most list and watch requests are served from this in-memory cache, which\n207:     dramatically reduces the load on etcd. Consistent reads are also served from the\n208:     cache. This is achieved by first fetching the revision number of the latest write from\n209:     etcd. The server then ensures the cache is at least that recent\u2014waiting for it to\n210:     refresh if necessary\u2014before serving the request.\n211: *   **Fallback to Storage:** If a client request cannot be served from the\n212:     cache's buffer, the request \"falls through\" to the underlying etcd storage.\n213: *   **Bookmarks:** The cacher uses bookmark events to track the latest `ResourceVersion` for\n214:     unchanged objects. This prevents the cache's `ResourceVersion` from becoming too old,\n215:     which avoids the need for expensive relist operations from etcd when the objects have\n216:     not been modified.\n217: \n218: ## 5. Conflict Resolution\n219: \n220: *   **Optimistic Concurrency via `resourceVersion`:** Clients are expected to perform updates using a\n221:     read-modify-write workflow. The apiserver uses the `resourceVersion` field of every\n222:     object to enforce optimistic concurrency. This `resourceVersion` is not an arbitrary number;\n223:     it maps directly to etcd's globally consistent `mod_revision`. When a client submits an\n224:     update (`PUT` or `PATCH`), it must provide the `resourceVersion` of the object it based its\n225:     modifications on. If the `resourceVersion` on the server does not match the current\n226:     `mod_revision` in etcd, the server rejects the request with a `409 Conflict` error. This\n227:     forces the client to re-read the object, resolve the conflict, and resubmit with the new\n228:     `resourceVersion`.\n229: *   **Server-Side Apply:** A declarative, \"intent-based\" patch. The server maintains a\n230:     `managedFields` section in the object's metadata to track which \"manager\" (e.g., a\n231:     controller) owns each field. This allows multiple actors to manage different parts of the\n232:     same object without overwriting each other's changes.\n233: \n234: ## 6. Discovery and OpenAPI\n235: \n236: Apiservers serve the `/apis` discovery endpoints and the `/openapi/v2` and `/openapi/v3`\n237: specifications. The generation of the OpenAPI specification is a multi-stage process.\n238: \n239: *   **`openapi-gen`**: This tool reflects on Go structs, reads godoc comments, and looks at\n240:     validation struct tags to generate a map of all API definitions.\n241: *   **`zz_generated.openapi.go`**: The output is a large Go file containing a\n242:     `GetOpenAPIDefinitions` function.\n243: *   **Runtime**: The `GenericAPIServer` calls this generated function to build the final OpenAPI\n244:     JSON spec that it serves to clients.\n245: \n246: ## 7. Security & Observability\n247: \n248: *   **Audit (`pkg/audit`):** The apiserver has a policy-driven event logging pipeline. The audit\n249:     policy controls what is logged and at which stage of a request.\n250: *   **Security:**\n251:     *   **mTLS:** The primary authentication mechanism for system components.\n252:     *   **Service Account Token Issuance:** The `kube-apiserver` acts as an OIDC provider,\n253:         issuing and validating JWTs for `ServiceAccount`s.\n254: \n255: ## 8. Streaming Protocols\n256: \n257: *   **Websockets:** The apiserver uses websockets to upgrade HTTP\n258:     connections for interactive, streaming protocols like `exec`, `attach`, and\n259:     `port-forward`. The `UpgradeAwareProxyHandler` manages this process.\n260: ",
    "url": "https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0@8c9c67c000104450cfc5a5f48053a9a84b73cf93/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/ARCHITECTURE.md"

This is a different resource, scoped to the parent resource, but it may have a different kind.\\n41: \\t// For instance, /pods has the resource \\\"pods\\\" and the kind \\\"Pod\\\", while /pods/foo/status has the resource \\\"pods\\\", the sub resource \\\"status\\\", and the kind \\\"Pod\\\"\\n42: \\t// (because status operates on pods). This is to prevent\\n49: \\t// admission controllers with side effects and a method of reconciliation from being overwhelmed.\\n50: \\t// However, a value of false for this does not mean that the modification will be persisted, because it\\n51: \\t// could still be rejected by a subsequent validation step.\\n52: \\tIsDryRun() bool\\n53: \\t// GetObject is the object from the incoming request prior to default values being applied\\n54: \\tGetObject() runtime.Object\\n55: \\t// GetOldObject is the existing object. It must be specified.\\n78: // It is usually provided automatically based on your strategy.\\n79: type Scoper interface {\\n80: \\t// NamespaceScoped returns true if the storage is namespaced\\n81: \\tNamespaceScoped() bool\\n82: }\\n83: \\n84: // KindProvider specifies a different kind for its API than for its internal storage. For such objects, there is no in-memory representation for\\n86: // the object, so they must be represented as generic objects (e.g. runtime.Unknown), but when we present the object as part of\\n87: // API discovery we want to present the specific kind, not the generic internal representation.\\n88: type KindProvider interface {\\n89: \\tKind() string\\n90: }\\n91: \\n92: // ShortNamesProvider is an interface for RESTful storage services. those that operate\n36: // on collections and those that operate on individually named items.\n37: // Collection interfaces:\n38: // (Method: Current -> Proposed)\n39: //    GET: Lister -> CollectionGetter\n40: //    WATCH: Watcher -> CollectionWatcher\n41: //    CREATE: Creater -> CollectionCreater\n42: //    DELETE: (n/a) -> CollectionDeleter\n43: //    UPDATE: (n/a) -> CollectionUpdater\n44: //\n45: // Single item interfaces:\n46: // (Method: Current -> Proposed)\n47: //    GET: Getter -> NamedGetter\n48: //    WATCH: (n/a) -> NamedWatcher\n49: //    CREATE: (n/a) -> NamedCreater\n50: //    DELETE: Deleter -> NamedDeleter\n51: //    UPDATE: Update -> NamedUpdater\n52: \n53: // Storage is a generic interface for RESTful storage services.\n54: // Resources which are exported to the RESTful API of apiserver need to implement this interface. It is expected\n55: // that objects may implement any of the below interfaces.\n56: //\n57: // Consider using StorageWithReadiness whenever possible.\n58: type Storage interface {\n59: \t// New returns an empty object that can be used with Create and Update after request data has been put into it.\n60: \t// This object must be a pointer type for use with Codec.DecodeInto([]byte, runtime.Object)\n61: \tNew() runtime.Object\n62: \n63: \t// Destroy cleans up its resources on shutdown.\n64: \t// Destroy has to be implemented in thread-safe way and be prepared\n65: \t// for being called more than once.\n66: \tDestroy()\n67: }\n68: \n69: // StorageWithReadiness extends Storage interface with the readiness check.\n70: type StorageWithReadiness interface {\n71: \tStorage\n72: \n73: \t// ReadinessCheck allows for checking storage readiness.\n74: \tReadinessCheck() error\n75: }\n76: \n77: // Scoper indicates what scope the resource is at. For such objects, there is no in-memory representation for\n86: // the object, so they must be represented as generic objects (e.g. runtime.Unknown), but when we present the object as part of\n87: // API discovery we want to present the specific kind, not the generic internal representation.\n88: type KindProvider interface {\n89: \tKind() string\n90: }\n91: \n92: // ShortNamesProvider is an interface for RESTful storage services. {
  "content": "# Kubernetes API Server Library: Subsystem Architecture and Extension Guide\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\nThe `k8s.io/apiserver` library (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/`) is the reusable foundation upon which every Kubernetes API server is built. It is not the full `kube-apiserver` binary\u2014it is the generic scaffolding that provides the HTTP serving infrastructure, request filtering pipeline, type-system integration, storage abstraction, and security plumbing. A consumer of this library instantiates a `GenericAPIServer`, attaches REST storage implementations behind `APIGroupInfo` descriptors, and gets a standards-compliant Kubernetes API surface for free.\n\n### Upstream Dependencies\n\nThe library sits on top of:\n\n- **`k8s.io/apimachinery`** \u2014 type system primitives (`runtime.Scheme`, `runtime.Object`, `GroupVersionKind`, codec infrastructure, field/label selectors)\n- **`k8s.io/client-go`** \u2014 informers and the REST client used by the loopback client and optional webhook callers\n- **etcd (via `go.etcd.io/etcd/client/v3`)** \u2014 the sole officially-supported storage backend, accessed through `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/etcd3/`\n- **`k8s.io/kube-openapi`** \u2014 OpenAPI v2/v3 spec generation and serving\n\n### Downstream Consumers\n\n- **`kube-apiserver` core** (`pkg/controlplane/`) \u2014 registers built-in API groups by calling `GenericAPIServer.InstallLegacyAPIGroup` / `InstallAPIGroups`\n- **`kube-aggregator`** \u2014 builds an aggregation-layer server on top of the library\n- **`apiextensions-apiserver`** \u2014 uses the library to serve CRDs\n- **Extension API servers** built with `apiserver-builder` or manually using `RecommendedOptions`\n\n### Boundaries\n\nThe library handles everything between network bytes and your storage call: TLS termination, authentication, authorization, flow control, serialisation, admission, versioning, and watch fan-out. It does **not** own cluster-level policy (that is RBAC controller code in `pkg/`), controller logic, or the etcd cluster itself.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\nThe directory structure maps almost one-to-one to functional responsibility:\n\n| Directory | Primary Responsibility |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/server/` | Server bootstrap: `Config`, `GenericAPIServer`, handler chain wiring, lifecycle signals, hooks |\n| `pkg/server/options/` | CLI flag binding; `RecommendedOptions` composes all option groups for extension API servers |\n| `pkg/endpoints/` | HTTP-level dispatch: `APIInstaller`, verb handlers (`create.go`, `get.go`, `patch.go`, `watch.go`), filters |\n| `pkg/registry/rest/` | REST storage interfaces (`rest.Storage`, `Getter`, `Creater`, `Updater`, etc.) |\n| `pkg/registry/generic/registry/` | Generic `Store` struct implementing CRUD+Watch on top of `storage.Interface` |\n| `pkg/storage/` | Storage interface definition and `Versioner` abstraction |\n| `pkg/storage/cacher/` | In-memory watch cache (`Cacher`, `watchCache`, `cacheWatcher`) |\n| `pkg/storage/etcd3/` | etcd3 implementation of `storage.Interface` |\n| `pkg/admission/` | Admission plugin interfaces, chain, plugin registry, initializers |\n| `pkg/authentication/` | Pluggable authenticator chain |\n| `pkg/authorization/` | Pluggable authorizer chain |\n| `pkg/audit/` | Policy-driven audit event pipeline |\n| `pkg/util/flowcontrol/` | API Priority and Fairness (APF): `FlowSchema`, `PriorityLevel`, work estimator |\n\n### The `GenericAPIServer` and `Config`\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go` contains the `GenericAPIServer` struct: the central object at runtime. It owns the `APIServerHandler` (the full HTTP handler chain), the discovery endpoint managers, health check registries, the audit backend, and the `delegationTarget` pointer for the server chain.\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go` holds the `Config` struct, which is populated from option structs and then \"completed\" (via `Config.Complete()`) before being used to construct the server. Default values are set in `NewConfig`:\n\n```go\n// config.go:427-478\nreturn &Config{\n    BuildHandlerChainFunc:          DefaultBuildHandlerChain,\n    MaxRequestsInFlight:            400,\n    MaxMutatingRequestsInFlight:    200,\n    RequestTimeout:                 time.Duration(60) * time.Second,\n    JSONPatchMaxCopyBytes:          int64(3 * 1024 * 1024),\n    MaxRequestBodyBytes:            int64(3 * 1024 * 1024),\n    ...\n}\n```\n\nThe field `BuildHandlerChainFunc` is the primary extension point for the filter pipeline\u2014it defaults to `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` but callers may replace it entirely.\n\n### `APIGroupInfo` and REST Storage Registration\n\nAn API group is attached to the server by constructing an `APIGroupInfo` and calling `InstallAPIGroups`:\n\n```go\n// genericapiserver.go:71-98\ntype APIGroupInfo struct {\n    PrioritizedVersions          []schema.GroupVersion\n    VersionedResourcesStorageMap map[string]map[string]rest.Storage\n    Scheme                       *runtime.Scheme\n    NegotiatedSerializer         runtime.NegotiatedSerializer\n    ParameterCodec               runtime.ParameterCodec\n    ...\n}\n```\n\nThe `VersionedResourcesStorageMap` maps `version \u2192 resource-name \u2192 rest.Storage`. `InstallAPIGroups` (`genericapiserver.go:876`) iterates the versions, calls `installAPIResources`, and registers discovery handlers. `InstallLegacyAPIGroup` does the same for the `/api` (core) prefix.\n\n### The `Store` \u2014 Generic CRUD Engine\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go` contains the `Store` struct, which is the standard CRUD/Watch implementation. Every built-in resource embeds a `Store`. It delegates to a `DryRunnableStorage` (wrapping `storage.Interface`) and enforces business logic through strategy objects:\n\n```go\n// store.go:100-248 (selected fields)\ntype Store struct {\n    CreateStrategy rest.RESTCreateStrategy\n    UpdateStrategy rest.RESTUpdateStrategy\n    DeleteStrategy rest.RESTDeleteStrategy\n    BeginCreate    BeginCreateFunc   // optional \"transaction\" hook\n    AfterCreate    AfterCreateFunc   // optional post-create hook\n    BeginUpdate    BeginUpdateFunc\n    AfterUpdate    AfterUpdateFunc\n    AfterDelete    AfterDeleteFunc\n    Decorator      func(runtime.Object) // exit hook after storage read\n    Storage        DryRunnableStorage\n    ...\n}\n```\n\nStrategies carry the actual business logic (field immutability, name generation, namespace defaulting, validation). The `Store` itself is storage-agnostic; it calls the strategy before writing and after reading.\n\n### The `APIServerHandler` \u2014 Routing Architecture\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/handler.go` describes the dual-routing system:\n\n```\nFullHandlerChain \u2192 Director \u2192 GoRestfulContainer (API paths)\n                            \u2192 NonGoRestfulMux    (utility paths: /healthz, /metrics, /openapi)\n```\n\n`GoRestfulContainer` (from `github.com/emicklei/go-restful`) handles structured REST API routing with content negotiation. `NonGoRestfulMux` is a simple `PathRecorderMux` for everything else. The `Director` inspects the incoming path to decide which branch to use.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n\nThis section traces a `kubectl create deployment` (a `POST /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/default/deployments`) through the full stack.\n\n### Phase 1: Outer Filter Chain (`DefaultBuildHandlerChain`)\n\nThe filter chain is assembled inside-out (wrappers applied in reverse order of the listed sequence). The code in `config.go:1015-1096` shows the exact wrap order. When a request arrives, it traverses these filters from outermost to innermost:\n\n1. **`WithAuditInit`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/audit_init.go`) \u2014 allocates an audit event for the request.\n2. **`WithPanicRecovery`** (`pkg/server/filters/wrap.go`) \u2014 catches panics, converts them to 500s.\n3. **`WithMuxAndDiscoveryComplete`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/mux_discovery_complete.go`) \u2014 blocks requests until all API paths are installed (prevents spurious 404s at startup).\n4. **`WithRequestReceivedTimestamp`** \u2014 stamps the request receipt time.\n5. **`WithRequestInfo`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go`) \u2014 parses the URL into a `RequestInfo` struct (verb, resource, namespace, name) and injects it into the context.\n6. **`WithRoutine`** (optional, feature-gated) \u2014 executes downstream handlers in a new goroutine to minimize stack depth.\n7. **`WithLatencyTrackers`** / **`WithHTTPLogging`** \u2014 metrics and structured logging.\n8. **`WithRetryAfter`** (optional) \u2014 rejects new requests with HTTP 429 during graceful shutdown.\n9. **`WithHSTS`** / **`WithCacheControl`** \u2014 response header policies.\n10. **`WithProbabilisticGoaway`** (optional) \u2014 probabilistically sends `GOAWAY` on HTTP/2 connections to trigger client reconnection and load rebalancing.\n11. **`WithWatchTerminationDuringShutdown`** / **`WithWaitGroup`** \u2014 tracks in-flight requests for graceful drain; rate-limits watch draining during shutdown.\n12. **`WithRequestDeadline`** \u2014 applies the request timeout from `Config.RequestTimeout` (default 60s) to the context.\n13. **`WithTimeoutForNonLongRunningRequests`** \u2014 enforces the deadline by running downstream in a goroutine and returning a timeout response if the deadline is exceeded.\n14. **`WithWarningRecorder`** \u2014 thread-safe buffer for adding warning headers to the response.\n15. **`WithAuthentication`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go`) \u2014 runs the authenticator chain; on failure, invokes the `failedHandler` which returns `401 Unauthorized`.\n16. **`WithTracing`** (optional, feature-gated) \u2014 starts an OpenTelemetry span; placed after authn so clients can influence sampling.\n17. **`WithAudit`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go`) \u2014 populates audit event with user identity and response status.\n18. **`WithImpersonation`** / **`WithConstrainedImpersonation`** \u2014 checks and applies user impersonation (`Impersonate-*` headers).\n19. **`WithPriorityAndFairness`** or **`WithMaxInFlightLimit`** \u2014 either APF-based flow control (classifies request into a `FlowSchema`/`PriorityLevel` queue) or the simpler fixed limit (`MaxRequestsInFlight=400`, `MaxMutatingRequestsInFlight=200`).\n20. **`WithAuthorization`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go`) \u2014 invokes the authorizer chain; returns `403 Forbidden` on denial.\n\nAt this point the request is authenticated, authorized, and admitted through flow control. The body has still **not** been deserialized.\n\n### Phase 2: REST Endpoint Handler (`pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go`)\n\nThe `APIInstaller` (`pkg/endpoints/installer.go`) registered an HTTP handler for `POST /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/deployments` when `InstallAPIGroups` was called. That handler is `createHandler` in `pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go`.\n\nInside `createHandler`:\n\n1. **Content negotiation** \u2014 selects the input and output serializer based on `Content-Type` / `Accept` headers (`negotiation.NegotiateInputSerializer`).\n2. **Body read** \u2014 `limitedReadBodyWithRecordMetric` reads up to `MaxRequestBodyBytes` (3 MiB by default).\n3. **Decode** \u2014 `scope.Serializer.DecoderToVersion(decodeSerializer, scope.HubGroupVersion)` converts the wire JSON/YAML/protobuf bytes into the internal version of the object via the `Scheme`'s hub-and-spoke conversion.\n4. **Field validation** \u2014 if `FieldValidation=Warn` or `Strict`, a strict decoder is used and unknown fields produce warnings or errors.\n5. **Admission (mutation phase)** \u2014 `admission.NewAttributesRecord(obj, ...)` creates the `Attributes` package; `requestFunc` wraps the final storage call. The field manager (`FieldManager.UpdateNoErrors`) sets `managedFields`.\n6. **`finisher.FinishRequest`** \u2014 runs the actual storage call and admission in a dedicated goroutine with the request context deadline.\n7. **Admission (validation phase)** \u2014 `ManagedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController` validates field manager annotations; then the generic admission chain's `Validate` pass runs.\n8. **Storage write** \u2014 `r.Create(ctx, name, obj, validateFunc, options)` calls the `Store.Create` method, which invokes `CreateStrategy.PrepareForCreate`, `CreateStrategy.Validate`, then `Storage.Create` to write to etcd via `GuaranteedUpdate` (or the cacher).\n9. **Response** \u2014 the stored object is serialized to the negotiated output format and written to `http.ResponseWriter`.\n\n### Phase 3: Storage Layer\n\nThe storage call descends through:\n\n```\nStore.Storage (DryRunnableStorage)\n  \u2192 cacher.Cacher (implements storage.Interface)\n      \u2192 etcd3.store (implements storage.Interface)\n          \u2192 etcd grpc client\n```\n\nFor **writes**, the cacher delegates directly to the etcd3 store. For **reads and watches**, the cacher serves from its in-memory `watchCache` where possible.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Watch Cache Architecture\n\nThe watch cache (`pkg/storage/cacher/`) is fundamental to Kubernetes scalability. Without it, every controller's `WATCH` call would hit etcd directly, creating an unbounded fan-out.\n\n### Structure\n\n- **`Cacher`** (`cacher.go:262`) \u2014 the top-level struct; implements `storage.Interface` and acts as a transparent proxy, intercepting `Watch` and `List` calls.\n- **`watchCache`** (`watch_cache.go`) \u2014 an ordered ring buffer of recent `watchCacheEvent`s, plus a snapshot store of all current objects for list serving.\n- **`cacheWatcher`** (`cache_watcher.go`) \u2014 one instance per active client watch; receives events from the `Cacher`'s dispatch loop and filters them against the client's label/field selectors.\n\n### Initialization Sequence\n\n1. At startup, the `Cacher` performs a full `LIST` of its resource from etcd to populate the `watchCache` snapshot.\n2. It records the `resourceVersion` from the list response.\n3. It starts a background `WATCH` from that version, feeding events into the `incoming` channel (`cacher.go:268`).\n4. A dispatch goroutine reads from `incoming`, updates the `watchCache` ring buffer, and fans out to all registered `cacheWatcher` instances.\n5. The `ready` gate (`cacher.go:280`) blocks any client `List` or `Watch` until the initial list is complete.\n\n### Bookmark Events\n\nThe cacher sends `BOOKMARK` events to each `cacheWatcher` to keep the `resourceVersion` field current even when no mutations are occurring. This prevents clients from drifting to a stale `resourceVersion` that would require a full `RELIST` from etcd on reconnect. Bookmarks are scheduled via `watcherBookmarkTimeBuckets` (`cacher.go:198`), with a default frequency of 1 minute (`defaultBookmarkFrequency`).\n\n### Consistent Reads from Cache\n\nFor consistent reads (the default since 1.31), the cacher first fetches the current `mod_revision` from etcd (a cheap point-read), then waits for its cache to be at least that version before serving. This avoids stale reads without requiring a full etcd round-trip.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Server Composition: The Delegation Chain\n\nThe `kube-apiserver` binary composes three `GenericAPIServer` instances into a delegation chain. The `DelegationTarget` interface (`config.go:306-337`) defines how one server hands off to the next:\n\n```\nAggregator Server\n    \u2193 (delegate)\nKube API Server (core)\n    \u2193 (delegate)\nAPI Extensions Server (CRDs)\n    \u2193 (delegate)\nemptyDelegate (returns 404)\n```\n\nEach server's `Handler.Director` checks its own registered routes. On a miss, `UnprotectedHandler()` (`genericapiserver.go:339`) returns the delegate server's `Director` as a fallback. This gives the aggregation layer first pick for extension API service paths, core APIs are handled next, and CRDs last.\n\nThe composition is wired in `cmd/kube-apiserver/app/server.go`'s `CreateServerChain`.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Admission Control\n\nAdmission control lives in `pkg/admission/`. The key interfaces (`interfaces.go:122-173`) are:\n\n```go\ntype MutationInterface interface {\n    Interface\n    Admit(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) error\n}\n\ntype ValidationInterface interface {\n    Interface\n    Validate(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) error\n}\n```\n\nThe `chainAdmissionHandler` (`chain.go`) iterates the registered plugins in order. Mutation (`Admit`) runs first across all mutating plugins, then validation (`Validate`) runs across all validating plugins. A plugin declares which operations it handles via `Handles(operation Operation) bool`.\n\n### Admission Attributes\n\n`Attributes` (`interfaces.go:31-77`) is the interface passed to every plugin. It provides the object being created/updated, the old object (for updates/deletes), the GVK, the user info, dry-run status, and a mutable annotation map written to the audit log. Critically, `GetObject()` returns the already-decoded in-memory object\u2014admission is the first and only stage where the body is materialized.\n\n### Reinvocation\n\nThe admission chain supports reinvocation: if a mutating plugin sets `ShouldReinvoke()` on the `ReinvocationContext`, the entire mutation chain is re-run. This handles the case where plugin B depends on field state that plugin A sets.\n\n### Webhook Support\n\nThe `plugin/` directory under `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/` contains the `MutatingAdmissionWebhook` and `ValidatingAdmissionWebhook` plugins. They serialize the `AdmissionReview` object, POST it to an external webhook endpoint, and interpret the response. Webhook plugins are themselves `MutationInterface`/`ValidationInterface` implementations that participate in the same chain.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Authentication and Authorization\n\n### Authentication (`pkg/authentication/`)\n\nThe authenticator chain is a union of configured authenticators (`request/union/`). The first authenticator to return a non-nil `user.Info` wins. Common implementations include:\n- `x509` \u2014 client certificate validation against a CA bundle\n- `bearertoken` \u2014 validates a token string (delegates to a `TokenAuthenticator`)\n- OIDC \u2014 validates JWTs from an external provider\n- Service account tokens \u2014 issued by the apiserver's own OIDC-like endpoint\n\nThe authenticator is wired into the filter chain at `config.go:1056`:\n```go\nhandler = genericapifilters.WithAuthentication(handler, c.Authentication.Authenticator, failedHandler, ...)\n```\n\n### Authorization (`pkg/authorization/`)\n\nThe authorizer chain uses a union-or-default pattern with three possible responses per authorizer: `Allow`, `Deny`, or `NoOpinion`. `NoOpinion` passes the request to the next authorizer. `Deny` short-circuits immediately. Only if all authorizers return `NoOpinion` is the request denied.\n\n---\n\n## 8. API Priority and Fairness (APF)\n\nWhen `FlowControl` is configured, `WithPriorityAndFairness` (`pkg/server/filters/priority-and-fairness.go`) replaces the simpler `WithMaxInFlightLimit`. APF:\n\n1. Classifies the request into a `FlowSchema` using the subject (user/group/service account) and resource.\n2. Assigns the request to a `PriorityLevel` queue.\n3. Estimates the request's \"work\" (`flowcontrolrequest.WorkEstimator`) based on the resource type and count of objects in storage.\n4. Queues the request if the queue is full, or rejects it with HTTP 429 if the queue length limit is exceeded.\n\nThe work estimator uses `StorageObjectCountTracker.Get` to read the number of objects of a given type from the cache, enabling proportional queue sizing. The default fallback is the simple `WithMaxInFlightLimit` with limits of 400 read and 200 mutating requests.\n\n---\n\n## 9. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 9.1 `BuildHandlerChainFunc` \u2014 Filter Pipeline Replacement\n\n```go\n// config.go:429\nBuildHandlerChainFunc: DefaultBuildHandlerChain,\n```\n\nReplacing this function allows embedding servers to add custom middleware globally or to disable specific standard filters. The function signature is `func(http.Handler, *Config) http.Handler`. **Risk**: omitting a standard filter (e.g., authorization) can create security holes. Adding filters that block or panic can make the server unresponsive.\n\n### 9.2 `PostStartHooks` and `PreShutdownHooks`\n\n```go\n// hooks.go:43-46\ntype PostStartHookFunc func(context PostStartHookContext) error\ntype PreShutdownHookFunc func() error\n```\n\nAdded via `Config.AddPostStartHook`. These run asynchronously in separate goroutines after the server starts listening. They receive a `PostStartHookContext` with a `LoopbackClientConfig` for authenticated self-calls. **Risk**: a hook that never completes or panics will consume a goroutine indefinitely; hooks that conflict (e.g., two hooks writing the same Lease) must implement their own coordination.\n\n### 9.3 Health and Readiness Checks\n\n```go\n// config.go:570-580\nfunc (c *Config) AddHealthChecks(healthChecks ...healthz.HealthChecker)\nfunc (c *Config) AddReadyzChecks(healthChecks ...healthz.HealthChecker)\n```\n\n`healthz.HealthChecker` is a simple interface with `Name() string` and `Check(*http.Request) error`. Extension servers commonly add checks for their own custom dependencies (e.g., a secondary datastore). A failing readiness check prevents traffic from load balancers without killing the process.\n\n### 9.4 REST Storage Interfaces \u2014 Capability Discovery\n\nThe `pkg/registry/rest/rest.go` file defines a rich set of optional interfaces:\n\n| Interface | Enables |\n|---|---|\n| `rest.Getter` | `GET /resource/{name}` |\n| `rest.Lister` | `GET /resource` |\n| `rest.Creater` | `POST /resource` |\n| `rest.Updater` | `PUT /resource/{name}` |\n| `rest.GracefulDeleter` | `DELETE /resource/{name}` with grace period |\n| `rest.Watcher` | `GET /resource?watch=true` |\n| `rest.Patcher` | `PATCH /resource/{name}` |\n| `rest.TableConvertor` | Tabular output for `kubectl get` |\n| `rest.StorageVersioner` | Storage version migration support |\n\nThe `APIInstaller` (`installer.go`) inspects the concrete storage object via type assertions at installation time to determine which HTTP verbs to register. Implementing only the interfaces you need keeps the API surface minimal.\n\n### 9.5 `Store` Hook Functions\n\nThe `Store` struct exposes several hooks that are called at specific points in the CRUD lifecycle:\n\n| Hook | Type | Called |\n|---|---|---|\n| `BeginCreate` | `BeginCreateFunc` | Before persistence; returns a commit/rollback func |\n| `AfterCreate` | `AfterCreateFunc` | After successful persistence, before `Decorator` |\n| `BeginUpdate` | `BeginUpdateFunc` | Before persistence |\n| `AfterUpdate` | `AfterUpdateFunc` | After successful persistence |\n| `AfterDelete` | `AfterDeleteFunc` | After deletion |\n| `Decorator` | `func(runtime.Object)` | After every read from storage |\n| `ShouldDeleteDuringUpdate` | `func(ctx, key, obj, existing) bool` | Whether an update should become a delete |\n\n**Risk**: the `Decorator` is called on every read including from list/watch results. Heavy computation here directly increases latency under load.\n\n### 9.6 Admission Plugins (`pkg/admission/`)\n\nAdding an admission plugin requires:\n1. Implementing `MutationInterface` and/or `ValidationInterface`.\n2. Registering it with the plugin registry (`admission/plugins.go`).\n3. Providing a `PluginInitializer` if the plugin needs shared resources (informers, clients).\n\n`RecommendedOptions.ExtraAdmissionInitializers` provides the hook for extension API servers to inject their own initializers.\n\n### 9.7 `RecommendedOptions` \u2014 Extension API Server Bootstrap\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/recommended.go` packages the most common configuration needs into a single struct:\n\n```go\ntype RecommendedOptions struct {\n    Etcd           *EtcdOptions\n    SecureServing  *SecureServingOptionsWithLoopback\n    Authentication *DelegatingAuthenticationOptions\n    Authorization  *DelegatingAuthorizationOptions\n    Audit          *AuditOptions\n    Features       *FeatureOptions\n    CoreAPI        *CoreAPIOptions\n    Admission      *AdmissionOptions\n    EgressSelector *EgressSelectorOptions\n    Traces         *TracingOptions\n}\n```\n\n`DelegatingAuthenticationOptions` and `DelegatingAuthorizationOptions` configure the server to delegate authn/authz decisions to the main `kube-apiserver` (via `SubjectAccessReview` and `TokenReview` APIs), which is the recommended pattern for extension servers.\n\n---\n\n## 10. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 10.1 etcd as the Single Point of Truth\n\nAll writes go through etcd. If etcd is unavailable:\n- Mutating requests fail immediately (the etcd client returns an error; `Store.Create/Update/Delete` propagates a 500 or 503).\n- Read requests _may_ still be served from the watch cache for `ResourceVersion=\"\"` (best-effort) or for consistent reads if the cache has a recent-enough `ResourceVersion`.\n- A prolonged etcd outage causes the watch cache to stall; the cacher's `ready` gate flips to `false` until the background watch reconnects and the cache is caught up.\n\n### 10.2 Watch Cache Memory Pressure\n\nThe `watchCache` ring buffer retains events for `DefaultEventFreshDuration` (75 seconds by default, `cacher.go:72`). The number of watchers is bounded by available goroutines and memory. Each `cacheWatcher` has an input buffer channel; if a slow client cannot drain events fast enough, the `cacheWatcher` terminates the watch (forcing the client to relist). In clusters with many resources and many controllers, memory for watch caches can be measured in gigabytes.\n\n### 10.3 Request Body Size Limits\n\nThe default `MaxRequestBodyBytes` is 3 MiB (`config.go:466`), matching the etcd recommended maximum. JSON payloads are larger than their proto equivalents; etcd stores proto. The comment in config explains the 2\u00d7 factor for JSON-to-proto conversion during write. Exceeding the limit returns HTTP 413.\n\n### 10.4 Optimistic Concurrency\n\nEvery object has a `resourceVersion` mapped to etcd's `mod_revision`. Updates must supply the current `resourceVersion`; a mismatch returns HTTP 409 Conflict. This is implemented in `storage/etcd3/store.go` using etcd's compare-and-swap (`txn(If(version == expected)).Then(Put(...))`). Clients must implement retry logic; the standard client-go `RetryOnConflict` helper exists for this.\n\n### 10.5 Handler Chain Construction Ordering\n\n`DefaultBuildHandlerChain` wraps handlers inside-out, so the last `handler = ...` line in the function executes first at request time (`WithAuditInit`). This ordering is subtle: tracing is placed _after_ authentication specifically to allow authenticated clients to influence sampling rates. Placing a filter in the wrong position (e.g., authorization before `WithRequestInfo` populates the context) would cause panics or incorrect behavior.\n\n### 10.6 Graceful Shutdown Sequencing\n\nThe `lifecycle_signals.go` file documents the shutdown protocol precisely:\n\n```\nT0:    SIGTERM received \u2192 ShutdownInitiated \u2192 /readyz returns red\nT0+70s: AfterShutdownDelayDuration \u2192 HTTP server stops accepting new connections\nT0+130s: InFlightRequestsDrained (up to 60s ShutdownTimeout)\n         \u2192 audit backend flushed \u2192 process exits\n```\n\nThe 70-second default `ShutdownDelayDuration` exists to allow load balancer health checks to propagate before connections are dropped. During this window the server is still fully functional. Extension servers should use this same pattern by calling `GenericAPIServer.RunUntil`.\n\n---\n\n## 11. Operational Implications\n\n### Performance\n\n- **Serialization is the dominant CPU cost** for high-QPS read paths. The library uses proto encoding to etcd (via `StorageVersioner`) and JSON/proto for HTTP responses. Content type negotiation happens per request; `Accept: application/vnd.kubernetes.protobuf` reduces serialization load significantly for high-volume clients (controllers).\n- **The `Decorator` hook runs on every read**. A `Decorator` that allocates or does I/O per object will dominate list latency for large collections. This is documented in `store.go:164`: \"_Decorator is intended for integrations that are above storage and should only be used for specific cases where storage of the value is not appropriate, since they cannot be watched._\"\n- **Admission adds latency proportional to the number of webhooks**. Each webhook call is a synchronous HTTP POST to an external endpoint. A webhook with P99 latency of 100ms on a frequently mutated resource (e.g., pods) adds 100ms to every create/update.\n\n### Reliability\n\n- **Webhook timeouts must be configured** on `ValidatingWebhookConfiguration.timeoutSeconds` and `MutatingWebhookConfiguration.timeoutSeconds`. The default is 10 seconds. A webhook that consistently times out will block all writes to the targeted resource. `failurePolicy: Ignore` avoids this at the cost of missing enforcement.\n- **APF misconfiguration is dangerous**. An overly restrictive `PriorityLevel` that starves `system` or `leader-election` priority classes can prevent the cluster from recovering from failures. APF configuration is itself stored in etcd, so a bootstrap deadlock is possible if the server cannot read its own flow control config.\n- **The `StorageReadinessHook`** (`server/storage_readiness_hook.go`) blocks the `readyz` endpoint until all registered storages report ready. Extension servers that register storage via `InstallAPIGroups` get this for free.\n\n### Maintainability\n\n- **Code-generating strategies reduces drift**. `deepcopy-gen`, `conversion-gen`, and `defaulter-gen` produce the boilerplate needed by the `Scheme`. Running generators on every type change is critical; skipping them causes runtime panics (nil pointer in DeepCopy) or silent data loss (missing conversion paths).\n- **`RecommendedOptions.ApplyTo` is the correct entry point** for extension servers, not raw `Config`. It applies sensible defaults and wires delegating authn/authz automatically.\n- **The hub-and-spoke version model** means every new API version requires an explicit conversion to/from the internal hub version. Failing to provide a conversion function causes HTTP 406 Not Acceptable when a client requests an unhandled version.\n\n---\n\n## 12. File and Directory Map\n\nThe following files are most important for understanding and extending the apiserver library:\n\n| File / Directory | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/ARCHITECTURE.md` | Official high-level architecture document with Mermaid diagrams |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go` | `Config` struct, `DefaultBuildHandlerChain`, server defaults |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go` | `GenericAPIServer`, `APIGroupInfo`, `InstallAPIGroups`, `DelegationTarget` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/handler.go` | `APIServerHandler` struct and dual-router architecture |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/hooks.go` | `PostStartHookFunc`, `PreShutdownHookFunc` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/lifecycle_signals.go` | Shutdown sequence documentation and signal types |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/recommended.go` | `RecommendedOptions` for extension API server bootstrap |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/installer.go` | `APIInstaller` \u2014 maps REST storage to HTTP routes |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go` | Full CREATE request lifecycle, admission, decode, storage |\n| engine, strategy hooks |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/interfaces.go` | `storage.Interface`, `Versioner`, `UpdateFunc` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/cacher.go` | `Cacher`, watch fan-out, bookmark scheduling |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/watch_cache.go` | Ring-buffer event store |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/etcd3/store.go` | etcd3 backend implementation |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/interfaces.go` | `MutationInterface`, `ValidationInterface`, `Attributes` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/chain.go` | `chainAdmissionHandler` iteration logic |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/filters/priority-and-fairness.go` | APF request dispatch |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/filters/maxinflight.go` | Simple in-flight limit fallback |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/filters/timeout.go` | Non-long-running request timeout enforcement |\n",
