{
  "content": "# Kubernetes API Server Library: Subsystem Architecture and Extension Guide\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\nThe `k8s.io/apiserver` library (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/`) is the reusable foundation upon which every Kubernetes API server is built. It is not the full `kube-apiserver` binary\u2014it is the generic scaffolding that provides the HTTP serving infrastructure, request filtering pipeline, type-system integration, storage abstraction, and security plumbing. A consumer of this library instantiates a `GenericAPIServer`, attaches REST storage implementations behind `APIGroupInfo` descriptors, and gets a standards-compliant Kubernetes API surface.\n\n### Upstream Dependencies\n\nThe library sits on top of:\n\n- **`k8s.io/apimachinery`** \u2014 type system primitives (`runtime.Scheme`, `runtime.Object`, `GroupVersionKind`, codec infrastructure, field/label selectors)\n- **`k8s.io/client-go`** \u2014 informers and the REST client used by the loopback client and optional webhook callers\n- **etcd (via `go.etcd.io/etcd/client/v3`)** \u2014 the sole officially-supported storage backend, accessed through `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/etcd3/`\n- **`k8s.io/kube-openapi`** \u2014 OpenAPI v2/v3 spec generation and serving\n\n### Downstream Consumers\n\n- **`kube-apiserver` core** (`pkg/controlplane/`) \u2014 registers built-in API groups by calling `GenericAPIServer.InstallLegacyAPIGroup` / `InstallAPIGroups`\n- **`kube-aggregator`** \u2014 builds the aggregation-layer server on top of the library\n- **`apiextensions-apiserver`** \u2014 uses the library to serve CRDs\n- **Extension API servers** built with `apiserver-builder` or manually using `RecommendedOptions`\n\n### Boundaries\n\nThe library handles everything between network bytes and your storage call: TLS termination, authentication, authorization, flow control, serialisation, admission, versioning, and watch fan-out. It does **not** own cluster-level policy (that is RBAC controller code in `pkg/`), controller logic, or the etcd cluster itself.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\nThe directory structure maps almost one-to-one to functional responsibility:\n\n| Directory | Primary Responsibility |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/server/` | Server bootstrap: `Config`, `GenericAPIServer`, handler chain wiring, lifecycle signals, hooks |\n| `pkg/server/options/` | CLI flag binding; `RecommendedOptions` composes all option groups for extension API servers |\n| `pkg/endpoints/` | HTTP-level dispatch: `APIInstaller`, verb handlers (`create.go`, `get.go`, `patch.go`, `watch.go`), filters |\n| `pkg/registry/rest/` | REST storage interfaces (`rest.Storage`, `Getter`, `Creater`, `Updater`, etc.) |\n| `pkg/registry/generic/registry/` | Generic `Store` struct implementing CRUD+Watch on top of `storage.Interface` |\n| `pkg/storage/` | Storage interface definition and `Versioner` abstraction |\n| `pkg/storage/cacher/` | In-memory watch cache (`Cacher`, `watchCache`, `cacheWatcher`) |\n| `pkg/storage/etcd3/` | etcd3 implementation of `storage.Interface` |\n| `pkg/admission/` | Admission plugin interfaces, chain, plugin registry, initializers |\n| `pkg/authentication/` | Pluggable authenticator chain |\n| `pkg/authorization/` | Pluggable authorizer chain |\n| `pkg/audit/` | Policy-driven audit event pipeline |\n| `pkg/util/flowcontrol/` | API Priority and Fairness (APF): `FlowSchema`, `PriorityLevel`, work estimator |\n\n### The `GenericAPIServer` and `Config`\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go` contains the `GenericAPIServer` struct: the central runtime object. It owns the `APIServerHandler` (the full HTTP handler tree), discovery endpoint managers, health check registries, the audit backend, and the `delegationTarget` pointer for the server chain.\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go` holds the `Config` struct, populated from option structs and then \"completed\" before constructing the server. Default values are set in `NewConfig`:\n\n```go\n// config.go:427-478\nreturn &Config{\n    BuildHandlerChainFunc:       DefaultBuildHandlerChain,\n    MaxRequestsInFlight:         400,\n    MaxMutatingRequestsInFlight: 200,\n    RequestTimeout:              time.Duration(60) * time.Second,\n    JSONPatchMaxCopyBytes:       int64(3 * 1024 * 1024),\n    MaxRequestBodyBytes:         int64(3 * 1024 * 1024),\n    ...\n}\n```\n\nThe field `BuildHandlerChainFunc` is the primary extension point for the filter pipeline\u2014it defaults to `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` but callers may replace it entirely.\n\n### `APIGroupInfo` and REST Storage Registration\n\nAn API group is attached to the server by constructing an `APIGroupInfo` and calling `InstallAPIGroups`:\n\n```go\n// genericapiserver.go:71-98\ntype APIGroupInfo struct {\n    PrioritizedVersions          []schema.GroupVersion\n    VersionedResourcesStorageMap map[string]map[string]rest.Storage\n    Scheme                       *runtime.Scheme\n    NegotiatedSerializer         runtime.NegotiatedSerializer\n    ParameterCodec               runtime.ParameterCodec\n    ...\n}\n```\n\nThe `VersionedResourcesStorageMap` maps `version \u2192 resource-name \u2192 rest.Storage`. `InstallAPIGroups` (`genericapiserver.go:876`) iterates the versions, calls `installAPIResources`, and registers discovery handlers. `InstallLegacyAPIGroup` does the same for the `/api` (core) prefix.\n\n### The `Store` \u2014 Generic CRUD Engine\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go` contains the `Store` struct, which is the standard CRUD/Watch implementation. Every built-in resource embeds a `Store`. It delegates to a `DryRunnableStorage` (wrapping `storage.Interface`) and enforces business logic through strategy objects:\n\n```go\n// store.go:100-248 (selected fields)\ntype Store struct {\n    CreateStrategy rest.RESTCreateStrategy\n    UpdateStrategy rest.RESTUpdateStrategy\n    DeleteStrategy rest.RESTDeleteStrategy\n    BeginCreate    BeginCreateFunc   // optional \"transaction\" hook\n    AfterCreate    AfterCreateFunc   // optional post-create hook\n    BeginUpdate    BeginUpdateFunc\n    AfterUpdate    AfterUpdateFunc\n    AfterDelete    AfterDeleteFunc\n    Decorator      func(runtime.Object) // exit hook after every storage read\n    Storage        DryRunnableStorage\n    ...\n}\n```\n\nStrategies carry the actual business logic (field immutability, name generation, namespace defaulting, validation). The `Store` itself is storage-agnostic; it invokes the strategy before writing and after reading.\n\n### The `APIServerHandler` \u2014 Routing Architecture\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/handler.go` describes the dual-routing system:\n\n```\nFullHandlerChain \u2192 Director \u2192 GoRestfulContainer (API paths)\n                            \u2192 NonGoRestfulMux    (utility paths: /healthz, /metrics, /openapi)\n```\n\n`GoRestfulContainer` (from `github.com/emicklei/go-restful`) handles structured REST API routing with content negotiation. `NonGoRestfulMux` is a simple `PathRecorderMux` for everything else. The `Director` inspects the incoming path to decide which branch to use.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n\nThis section traces a `kubectl create deployment` (`POST /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/default/deployments`) through the full stack.\n\n### Phase 1: Outer Filter Chain (`DefaultBuildHandlerChain`)\n\nThe filter chain is assembled inside-out: each `handler = WithX(handler, ...)` call wraps the existing handler in a new outer layer. The code in `config.go:1015-1096` shows the exact wrap order. When a request arrives, it traverses these filters from outermost to innermost:\n\n1. **`WithAuditInit`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/audit_init.go`) \u2014 allocates an audit event for the request.\n2. **`WithPanicRecovery`** (`pkg/server/filters/wrap.go`) \u2014 catches panics, converts them to 500s.\n3. **`WithMuxAndDiscoveryComplete`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/mux_discovery_complete.go`) \u2014 blocks requests until all API paths are installed (prevents spurious 404s at startup).\n4. **`WithRequestReceivedTimestamp`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/request_received_time.go`) \u2014 stamps the request receipt time into the context.\n5. **`WithRequestInfo`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go`) \u2014 parses the URL into a `RequestInfo` struct (verb, resource, namespace, name) and injects it into the context.\n6. **`WithRoutine`** (optional, feature-gated) \u2014 executes downstream handlers in a new goroutine to minimize stack depth.\n7. **`WithLatencyTrackers`** / **`WithHTTPLogging`** (`pkg/server/filters/`) \u2014 per-filter latency metrics and structured logging.\n8. **`WithRetryAfter`** (optional) \u2014 rejects new requests with HTTP 429 during graceful shutdown, adding `Retry-After: 1` and `Connection: close` headers.\n9. **`WithHSTS`** / **`WithCacheControl`** \u2014 response header policies.\n10. **`WithProbabilisticGoaway`** (optional) \u2014 probabilistically sends `GOAWAY` on HTTP/2 connections to trigger client reconnection and load rebalancing.\n11. **`WithWatchTerminationDuringShutdown`** / **`WithWaitGroup`** (`pkg/server/filters/waitgroup.go`) \u2014 tracks in-flight requests for graceful drain.\n12. **`WithRequestDeadline`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/request_deadline.go`) \u2014 applies the request timeout from `Config.RequestTimeout` (default 60s) to the context.\n13. **`WithTimeoutForNonLongRunningRequests`** (`pkg/server/filters/timeout.go`) \u2014 enforces the deadline by running downstream in a goroutine and returning a timeout response if the deadline is exceeded. Watch requests bypass this.\n14. **`WithWarningRecorder`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/warning.go`) \u2014 thread-safe buffer for adding warning headers to the response.\n15. **`WithAuthentication`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go`) \u2014 runs the authenticator chain; on failure, invokes the `failedHandler` which returns `401 Unauthorized`.\n16. **`WithTracing`** (optional, feature-gated) \u2014 starts an OpenTelemetry span; placed _after_ authn so clients can influence sampling rates.\n17. **`WithAudit`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go`) \u2014 populates the audit event with user identity and response status.\n18. **`WithImpersonation`** / **`WithConstrainedImpersonation`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/impersonation/`) \u2014 checks and applies user impersonation (`Impersonate-*` headers), re-running authorization with the impersonated identity.\n19. **`WithPriorityAndFairness`** or **`WithMaxInFlightLimit`** (`pkg/server/filters/priority-and-fairness.go` / `maxinflight.go`) \u2014 either APF-based flow control (classifies request into a `FlowSchema`/`PriorityLevel` queue) or the simpler fixed limit.\n20. **`WithAuthorization`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go`) \u2014 invokes the authorizer chain; returns `403 Forbidden` on denial.\n\nAt this point the request is authenticated, authorized, and admitted through flow control. The body has still **not** been deserialized.\n\n### Phase 2: REST Endpoint Handler (`pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go`)\n\nThe `APIInstaller` (`pkg/endpoints/installer.go`) registered an HTTP handler for `POST /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/deployments` when `InstallAPIGroups` was called. That handler is `createHandler` in `pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go`:\n\n1. **Content negotiation** \u2014 selects input and output serializer based on `Content-Type` / `Accept` headers (`negotiation.NegotiateInputSerializer`).\n2. **Body read** \u2014 `limitedReadBodyWithRecordMetric` reads up to `MaxRequestBodyBytes` (3 MiB default), recording the byte count as a metric.\n3. **Decode** \u2014 `scope.Serializer.DecoderToVersion(decodeSerializer, scope.HubGroupVersion)` converts the wire JSON/YAML/protobuf bytes into the _internal_ version of the object via the `Scheme`'s hub-and-spoke conversion graph.\n4. **Field validation** \u2014 if `FieldValidation=Warn` or `Strict`, a strict decoder detects and surfaces unknown fields.\n5. **Admission (mutation phase)** \u2014 `admission.NewAttributesRecord(obj, ...)` constructs the `Attributes` interface. The field manager (`FieldManager.UpdateNoErrors`) sets `managedFields`. The `requestFunc` wraps the final storage call and is passed to the admission chain so plugins can introspect the storage outcome.\n6. **`finisher.FinishRequest`** \u2014 runs the actual storage call and admission inside a dedicated goroutine with the request context deadline.\n7. **Admission (validation phase)** \u2014 `ManagedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController` validates field manager annotations; then the generic admission chain's `Validate` pass runs across all validating plugins.\n8. **Storage write** \u2014 `r.Create(ctx, name, obj, validateFunc, options)` calls `Store.Create`, which invokes `CreateStrategy.PrepareForCreate`, `CreateStrategy.Validate`, then `Storage.Create` to write to etcd.\n9. **Response** \u2014 the stored object is serialized to the negotiated output format and written to `http.ResponseWriter`.\n\n### Phase 3: Storage Layer\n\nThe storage call descends through:\n\n```\nStore.Storage (DryRunnableStorage)\n  \u2192 cacher.Cacher  (implements storage.Interface)\n      \u2192 etcd3.store  (implements storage.Interface)\n          \u2192 etcd gRPC client\n```\n\nFor **writes**, the cacher delegates directly to the etcd3 store. For **reads and watches**, the cacher serves from its in-memory `watchCache` where possible, falling back to etcd on a cache miss.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Watch Cache Architecture\n\nThe watch cache (`pkg/storage/cacher/`) is fundamental to Kubernetes scalability. Without it, every controller's `WATCH` call would hit etcd directly, creating an unbounded fan-out.\n\n### Structure\n\n- **`Cacher`** (`cacher.go:262`) \u2014 the top-level struct; implements `storage.Interface` and acts as a transparent proxy, intercepting `Watch` and `List` calls.\n- **`watchCache`** (`watch_cache.go`) \u2014 an ordered ring buffer of recent `watchCacheEvent`s, plus a snapshot store of all current objects used for list serving.\n- **`cacheWatcher`** (`cache_watcher.go`) \u2014 one instance per active client watch; receives events from the `Cacher`'s dispatch loop and filters them against the client's label/field selectors.\n- **`indexedWatchers`** (`cacher.go:142`) \u2014 a map that routes incoming events to exactly the set of watchers that need them, using field-indexed lookup to avoid scanning all watchers for every event.\n\n### Initialization Sequence\n\n1. At startup the `Cacher` performs a full `LIST` of its resource from etcd to populate the `watchCache` snapshot.\n2. It records the `resourceVersion` from the list response.\n3. It starts a background `WATCH` from that version, feeding events into the `incoming` channel (`cacher.go:268`).\n4. A dispatch goroutine reads from `incoming`, updates the ring buffer, and fans out to all registered `cacheWatcher` instances.\n5. The `ready` gate (`cacher.go:280`) blocks any client `List` or `Watch` until initialization is complete.\n\n### Bookmark Events\n\nThe cacher sends `BOOKMARK` events to each `cacheWatcher` to keep the `resourceVersion` current even when no mutations are occurring. This prevents clients from drifting to a stale version that would require a full re-LIST from etcd on reconnect. Bookmarks are scheduled via `watcherBookmarkTimeBuckets` (`cacher.go:198`), with a default frequency of 1 minute (`defaultBookmarkFrequency = time.Minute`).\n\n### Consistent Reads from Cache\n\nFor consistent reads, the cacher first fetches the current `mod_revision` from etcd (a cheap point-read), then waits for its cache to be at least that version before serving. This avoids stale reads without requiring a full etcd round-trip for data.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Server Composition: The Delegation Chain\n\nThe `kube-apiserver` binary composes three `GenericAPIServer` instances into a delegation chain. The `DelegationTarget` interface (`genericapiserver.go:306-337`) defines how one server hands off to the next:\n\n```\nAggregator Server\n    \u2193 (delegate)\nKube API Server (core)\n    \u2193 (delegate)\nAPI Extensions Server (CRDs)\n    \u2193 (delegate)\nemptyDelegate (returns 404)\n```\n\nEach server's `Handler.Director` checks its own registered routes. On a miss, `UnprotectedHandler()` returns the delegate server's `Director` as the fallback handler (`genericapiserver.go:339`). This gives the aggregation layer first pick for extension API service paths, core APIs are handled next, and CRDs last.\n\nWhen an incoming request arrives for `/apis/mycompany.com/v1/myresources`, the Aggregator checks whether an `APIService` has claimed that path. If so, it proxies the request to the backing service's IP. If not, the request falls through the delegation chain. This composition is wired in `cmd/kube-apiserver/app/server.go`'s `CreateServerChain`.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Admission Control\n\nAdmission control lives in `pkg/admission/`. The key interfaces (`interfaces.go:122-173`) are:\n\n```go\ntype MutationInterface interface {\n    Interface\n    Admit(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) error\n}\n\ntype ValidationInterface interface {\n    Interface\n    Validate(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) error\n}\n```\n\nThe `chainAdmissionHandler` (`chain.go:23`) iterates registered plugins in order. The `Admit` (mutation) pass runs first across all mutating plugins, then the `Validate` pass runs across all validating plugins. Each plugin declares which operations it handles via `Handles(operation Operation) bool`:\n\n```go\n// chain.go:31-43\nfunc (admissionHandler chainAdmissionHandler) Admit(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) error {\n    for _, handler := range admissionHandler {\n        if !handler.Handles(a.GetOperation()) { continue }\n        if mutator, ok := handler.(MutationInterface); ok {\n            if err := mutator.Admit(ctx, a, o); err != nil { return err }\n        }\n    }\n    return nil\n}\n```\n\n### Admission Attributes\n\n`Attributes` (`interfaces.go:31-77`) is the interface passed to every plugin. It provides the decoded in-memory object, the old object (for updates/deletes), the GVK, user info, dry-run status, and a mutable annotation map written to the audit log. Critically, `GetObject()` returns the already-decoded object \u2014 admission is the first stage where the body is materialized as a Go struct.\n\n### Reinvocation\n\nThe admission chain supports reinvocation: if a mutating plugin calls `ShouldReinvoke()` on the `ReinvocationContext`, the entire mutation chain re-runs. This handles the case where plugin B depends on a field state set by plugin A's mutation.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Authentication and Authorization\n\n### Authentication (`pkg/authentication/`)\n\nThe authenticator chain is a union of configured authenticators (`request/union/`). The first authenticator to return a non-nil `user.Info` wins. Common implementations include:\n- `x509` \u2014 client certificate validation against a CA bundle\n- `bearertoken` \u2014 validates a token string (delegates to a `TokenAuthenticator`)\n- OIDC \u2014 validates JWTs from an external provider\n- Service account tokens \u2014 issued by the apiserver's own OIDC-like endpoint\n\nThe authenticator is wired into the filter chain at `config.go:1056`:\n```go\nhandler = genericapifilters.WithAuthentication(\n    handler, c.Authentication.Authenticator, failedHandler, c.Authentication.APIAudiences, ...)\n```\n\n### Authorization (`pkg/authorization/`)\n\nThe authorizer chain uses a union-or-default model with three possible responses per authorizer: `Allow`, `Deny`, or `NoOpinion`. `NoOpinion` passes the request to the next authorizer. `Deny` short-circuits immediately. If all authorizers return `NoOpinion`, the request is denied.\n\n---\n\n## 8. API Priority and Fairness (APF)\n\nWhen `FlowControl` is configured (the default since 1.20+), `WithPriorityAndFairness` (`pkg/server/filters/priority-and-fairness.go`) replaces the simpler `WithMaxInFlightLimit`. APF:\n\n1. Classifies the request into a `FlowSchema` using the subject (user/group/service account) and resource type.\n2. Assigns the request to a `PriorityLevel` queue.\n3. Estimates the request's \"work\" (`flowcontrolrequest.WorkEstimator`) using the resource type and object count from `StorageObjectCountTracker.Get`.\n4. Queues the request if concurrency is saturated, or rejects with HTTP 429 if the queue length limit is exceeded.\n\nThe default fallback (`WithMaxInFlightLimit`) applies fixed limits of 400 read and 200 mutating concurrent requests (`config.go:443-444`).\n\n---\n\n## 9. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 9.1 `BuildHandlerChainFunc` \u2014 Filter Pipeline Replacement\n\n```go\n// config.go:429\nBuildHandlerChainFunc: DefaultBuildHandlerChain,\n```\n\nReplacing this function allows embedding servers to add custom middleware globally or to disable specific standard filters. The function signature is `func(http.Handler, *Config) http.Handler`. **Risk**: omitting a standard filter (e.g., authorization) creates security holes. Filters that panic or block make the server unresponsive.\n\n### 9.2 `PostStartHooks` and `PreShutdownHooks`\n\n```go\n// hooks.go:43-46\ntype PostStartHookFunc func(context PostStartHookContext) error\ntype PreShutdownHookFunc func() error\n```\n\nAdded via `Config.AddPostStartHook`. These run asynchronously in separate goroutines after the server starts listening. They receive a `PostStartHookContext` with a `LoopbackClientConfig` for authenticated self-calls. **Risk**: a hook that never completes consumes a goroutine indefinitely; hooks that conflict (e.g., two hooks writing the same Lease) must implement their own coordination.\n\n### 9.3 Health and Readiness Checks\n\n```go\n// config.go:570-580\nfunc (c *Config) AddHealthChecks(healthChecks ...healthz.HealthChecker)\nfunc (c *Config) AddReadyzChecks(healthChecks ...healthz.HealthChecker)\n```\n\n`healthz.HealthChecker` exposes `Name() string` and `Check(*http.Request) error`. Extension servers add checks for custom dependencies. A failing readiness check prevents load balancer traffic without killing the process. The `StorageReadinessHook` is registered automatically by `InstallAPIGroups` for all backing storages.\n\n### 9.4 REST Storage Interfaces \u2014 Capability Discovery\n\n`pkg/registry/rest/rest.go` defines a rich set of optional interfaces. The `APIInstaller` discovers capabilities at install time via type assertions:\n\n| Interface | Enables |\n|---|---|\n| `rest.Getter` | `GET /resource/{name}` |\n| `rest.Lister` | `GET /resource` |\n| `rest.Creater` | `POST /resource` |\n| `rest.Updater` | `PUT /resource/{name}` |\n| `rest.GracefulDeleter` | `DELETE /resource/{name}` with grace period |\n| `rest.Watcher` | `GET /resource?watch=true` |\n| `rest.Patcher` | `PATCH /resource/{name}` |\n| `rest.TableConvertor` | Tabular output for `kubectl get` |\n| `rest.StorageVersioner` | Storage version migration support |\n\nImplementing only the interfaces you need keeps the API surface minimal and avoids registering unsupported HTTP verbs.\n\n### 9.5 `Store` Hook Functions\n\nThe `Store` struct exposes lifecycle hooks called at specific points in the CRUD path:\n\n| Hook | Type | Called when |\n|---|---|---|\n| `BeginCreate` | `BeginCreateFunc` | Before persistence; returns a commit/rollback func |\n| `AfterCreate` | `AfterCreateFunc` | After successful persistence, before `Decorator` |\n| `BeginUpdate` | `BeginUpdateFunc` | Before persistence |\n| `AfterUpdate` | `AfterUpdateFunc` | After successful persistence |\n| `AfterDelete` | `AfterDeleteFunc` | After deletion |\n| `Decorator` | `func(runtime.Object)` | After every read from storage |\n| `ShouldDeleteDuringUpdate` | `func(ctx, key, obj, existing) bool` | Whether an update should become a delete |\n\n**Risk**: the `Decorator` runs on every read including list and watch results. As documented in `store.go:164`, it \"_cannot be watched_\" and is \"_intended for integrations that are above storage_.\" Heavy computation here directly dominates list latency under load.\n\n### 9.6 Admission Plugins\n\nAdding an admission plugin requires:\n1. Implementing `MutationInterface` and/or `ValidationInterface`.\n2. Registering it with the plugin registry (`admission/plugins.go`).\n3. Providing a `PluginInitializer` (`admission/interfaces.go:159`) if the plugin needs shared resources (informers, clients).\n\n`RecommendedOptions.ExtraAdmissionInitializers` (`options/recommended.go:47`) provides the hook for extension API servers to inject their own initializers without touching the plugin registry.\n\n### 9.7 `RecommendedOptions` \u2014 Extension API Server Bootstrap\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/recommended.go` packages the most common configuration needs:\n\n```go\ntype RecommendedOptions struct {\n    Etcd           *EtcdOptions\n    SecureServing  *SecureServingOptionsWithLoopback\n    Authentication *DelegatingAuthenticationOptions\n    Authorization  *DelegatingAuthorizationOptions\n    Audit          *AuditOptions\n    Features       *FeatureOptions\n    CoreAPI        *CoreAPIOptions\n    Admission      *AdmissionOptions\n    EgressSelector *EgressSelectorOptions\n    Traces         *TracingOptions\n}\n```\n\n`DelegatingAuthenticationOptions` and `DelegatingAuthorizationOptions` configure the server to delegate authn/authz decisions to the main `kube-apiserver` (via `TokenReview` and `SubjectAccessReview` APIs), which is the recommended pattern for extension servers. Calling `RecommendedOptions.ApplyTo(config)` applies all of these in the correct dependency order.\n\n---\n\n## 10. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 10.1 etcd as the Single Source of Truth\n\nAll writes go through etcd. If etcd is unavailable:\n- Mutating requests fail immediately: the etcd client returns an error; `Store.Create/Update/Delete` propagates a 500 or 503.\n- Read requests _may_ still be served from the watch cache for `ResourceVersion=\"\"` (best-effort) reads. Consistent reads stall because the cacher cannot confirm freshness.\n- A prolonged etcd outage causes the watch cache to stall; the `ready` gate flips to `false` until the background watch reconnects and the cache catches up.\n\n### 10.2 Watch Cache Memory Pressure\n\nThe `watchCache` ring buffer retains events for `DefaultEventFreshDuration` (75 seconds by default, `cacher.go:72`). Each `cacheWatcher` has an input buffer channel; if a slow client cannot drain events fast enough, the `cacheWatcher` forcibly terminates the watch (forcing a client re-LIST). In large clusters with many resources and many controllers, the aggregate memory for all watch caches can reach multiple gigabytes.\n\n### 10.3 Request Body Size Limits\n\nThe default `MaxRequestBodyBytes` is 3 MiB (`config.go:466`), matching the etcd recommended maximum. JSON payloads are larger than their proto equivalents; the comment in config explains the 2\u00d7 factor for JSON-to-proto growth during write. Exceeding the limit returns HTTP 413. The related `JSONPatchMaxCopyBytes` limit (also 3 MiB) bounds the total data movement in a JSON Merge Patch.\n\n### 10.4 Optimistic Concurrency\n\nEvery object's `resourceVersion` maps to etcd's `mod_revision`. Updates must supply the current `resourceVersion`; a mismatch returns HTTP 409 Conflict. This is implemented in `storage/etcd3/store.go` using etcd's compare-and-swap transaction. Clients must implement retry logic; the standard `client-go`'s `RetryOnConflict` helper addresses this.\n\n### 10.5 Handler Chain Construction Ordering\n\n`DefaultBuildHandlerChain` wraps handlers inside-out, so the last `handler = ...` line in the function (`WithAuditInit`) executes first at request time. This ordering is load-bearing: tracing is placed _after_ authentication specifically to allow authenticated clients to influence sampling rates. Placing a filter in the wrong position (e.g., authorization before `WithRequestInfo` populates the context) would cause nil-pointer panics or incorrect behavior.\n\n### 10.6 Graceful Shutdown Sequencing\n\n`lifecycle_signals.go` documents the shutdown protocol precisely:\n\n```\nT0:        SIGTERM received \u2192 ShutdownInitiated \u2192 /readyz returns red\n                              \u2192 PreShutdownHooks run\nT0+70s:    AfterShutdownDelayDuration:\n           \u2192 HTTP server stops accepting new connections\n           \u2192 Active long-running requests receive GOAWAY\nT0+130s:   InFlightRequestsDrained (up to 60s ShutdownTimeout)\n           \u2192 audit backend flushed \u2192 process exits\n```\n\nThe 70-second default `ShutdownDelayDuration` exists to allow load balancer health checks to propagate before connections are dropped. During this window the server continues to serve requests normally. When `ShutdownSendRetryAfter=true`, the server instead continues listening but replies to new requests with HTTP 429 + `Retry-After: 1`.\n\n---\n\n## 11. Operational Implications\n\n### Performance\n\n**Serialization is the dominant CPU cost** for high-QPS read paths. The library stores proto encoding in etcd (via `StorageVersioner`) and serves JSON/proto/CBOR over HTTP. Content-type negotiation happens per request; `Accept: application/vnd.kubernetes.protobuf` reduces serialization overhead significantly for high-volume clients such as controllers.\n\n**The `Decorator` hook runs on every read**. A `Decorator` that allocates or performs I/O per object will dominate list latency for large collections. As noted in `store.go:164`, it is intentionally limited to data that \"_cannot be watched_.\"\n\n**Admission adds latency proportional to webhook round-trips**. Each webhook call is a synchronous HTTP POST. A webhook with P99 latency of 100ms on a frequently mutated resource (e.g., pods) adds 100ms to every create/update. Webhook timeout and failure policy must be configured deliberately.\n\n### Reliability\n\n**Webhook `failurePolicy` is a sharp edge**. `failurePolicy: Fail` (the default for most built-in webhooks) means a webhook that consistently times out blocks all writes to the targeted resource. `failurePolicy: Ignore` avoids the block at the cost of missing enforcement when the webhook is down.\n\n**APF misconfiguration can cause cascading failures**. An overly restrictive `PriorityLevel` that starves `system` or `leader-election` priority classes can prevent the cluster from recovering from failures. APF configuration is itself stored in etcd, creating a potential bootstrap deadlock if the server cannot read its own flow control config on startup.\n\n**The `StorageReadinessHook`** blocks `/readyz` until all registered storages report ready. Extension servers that register storage via `InstallAPIGroups` get this check automatically, which prevents traffic from being sent to the server before it has a coherent view of etcd.\n\n### Maintainability\n\n**Code-generation reduces drift**. `deepcopy-gen`, `conversion-gen`, and `defaulter-gen` produce the boilerplate needed by the `Scheme`. Running generators on every type change is critical; skipping them causes runtime panics (nil pointer in `DeepCopy`) or silent data loss (missing conversion paths between versions).\n\n**`RecommendedOptions.ApplyTo` is the correct entry point** for extension servers. It applies sensible defaults and wires delegating authn/authz automatically. Using raw `Config` directly risks omitting security-critical defaults.\n\n**The hub-and-spoke version model** means every new API version requires an explicit conversion to/from the internal hub version. Failing to provide a conversion function causes HTTP 406 Not Acceptable when a client requests an unhandled version, which is a silent API regression.\n\n---\n\n## 12. File and Directory Map\n\nThe following files are most important for understanding and extending the apiserver library:\n\n| File / Directory | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/ARCHITECTURE.md` | Official high-level architecture document with Mermaid diagrams |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go` | `Config` struct, `DefaultBuildHandlerChain`, server defaults |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go` | `GenericAPIServer`, `APIGroupInfo`, `InstallAPIGroups`, `DelegationTarget` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/handler.go` | `APIServerHandler` struct and dual-router architecture |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/hooks.go` | `PostStartHookFunc`, `PreShutdownHookFunc` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/lifecycle_signals.go` | Shutdown sequence documentation and signal types |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/recommended.go` | `RecommendedOptions` for extension API server bootstrap |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/installer.go` | `APIInstaller` \u2014 maps REST storage to HTTP routes via type assertions |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go` | Full CREATE request lifecycle: decode, admission, storage write |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go` | Authentication filter |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go` | Authorization filter |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go` | URL \u2192 `RequestInfo` context injection |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/rest/rest.go` | All REST storage capability interfaces |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go` | `Store` CRUD+Watch engine, strategy hooks |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/interfaces.go` | `storage.Interface`, `Versioner`, `UpdateFunc` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/cacher.go` | `Cacher`, watch fan-out, bookmark scheduling |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/watch_cache.go` | Ring-buffer event store for the watch cache |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/etcd3/store.go` | etcd3 backend implementation |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/interfaces.go` | `MutationInterface`, `ValidationInterface`, `Attributes` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/chain.go` | `chainAdmissionHandler` iteration and reinvocation logic |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/filters/priority-and-fairness.go` | APF request dispatch |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/filters/maxinflight.go` | Simple in-flight limit fallback |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/filters/timeout.go` | Non-long-running request timeout enforcement |\n",
  "file_path": "/workspace/documentation.md"

{
  "content": "# Kubernetes API Server Library: Subsystem Architecture and Extension Guide\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\nThe `k8s.io/apiserver` library (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/`) is the reusable foundation upon which every Kubernetes API server is built. It is not the full `kube-apiserver` binary\u2014it is the generic scaffolding that provides the HTTP serving infrastructure, request filtering pipeline, type-system integration, storage abstraction, and security plumbing. A consumer of this library instantiates a `GenericAPIServer`, attaches REST storage implementations behind `APIGroupInfo` descriptors, and gets a standards-compliant Kubernetes API surface.\n\n### Upstream Dependencies\n\nThe library sits on top of:\n\n- **`k8s.io/apimachinery`** \u2014 type system primitives (`runtime.Scheme`, `runtime.Object`, `GroupVersionKind`, codec infrastructure, field/label selectors)\n- **`k8s.io/client-go`** \u2014 informers and the REST client used by the loopback client and optional webhook callers\n- **etcd (via `go.etcd.io/etcd/client/v3`)** \u2014 the sole officially-supported storage backend, accessed through `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/etcd3/`\n- **`k8s.io/kube-openapi`** \u2014 OpenAPI v2/v3 spec generation and serving\n\n### Downstream Consumers\n\n- **`kube-apiserver` core** (`pkg/controlplane/`) \u2014 registers built-in API groups by calling `GenericAPIServer.InstallLegacyAPIGroup` / `InstallAPIGroups`\n- **`kube-aggregator`** \u2014 builds the aggregation-layer server on top of the library\n- **`apiextensions-apiserver`** \u2014 uses the library to serve CRDs\n- **Extension API servers** built with `apiserver-builder` or manually using `RecommendedOptions`\n\n### Boundaries\n\nThe library handles everything between network bytes and your storage call: TLS termination, authentication, authorization, flow control, serialisation, admission, versioning, and watch fan-out. It does **not** own cluster-level policy (that is RBAC controller code in `pkg/`), controller logic, or the etcd cluster itself.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\nThe directory structure maps almost one-to-one to functional responsibility:\n\n| Directory | Primary Responsibility |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/server/` | Server bootstrap: `Config`, `GenericAPIServer`, handler chain wiring, lifecycle signals, hooks |\n| `pkg/server/options/` | CLI flag binding; `RecommendedOptions` composes all option groups for extension API servers |\n| `pkg/endpoints/` | HTTP-level dispatch: `APIInstaller`, verb handlers (`create.go`, `get.go`, `patch.go`, `watch.go`), filters |\n| `pkg/registry/rest/` | REST storage interfaces (`rest.Storage`, `Getter`, `Creater`, `Updater`, etc.) |\n| `pkg/registry/generic/registry/` | Generic `Store` struct implementing CRUD+Watch on top of `storage.Interface` |\n| `pkg/storage/` | Storage interface definition and `Versioner` abstraction |\n| `pkg/storage/cacher/` | In-memory watch cache (`Cacher`, `watchCache`, `cacheWatcher`) |\n| `pkg/storage/etcd3/` | etcd3 implementation of `storage.Interface` |\n| `pkg/admission/` | Admission plugin interfaces, chain, plugin registry, initializers |\n| `pkg/authentication/` | Pluggable authenticator chain |\n| `pkg/authorization/` | Pluggable authorizer chain |\n| `pkg/audit/` | Policy-driven audit event pipeline |\n| `pkg/util/flowcontrol/` | API Priority and Fairness (APF): `FlowSchema`, `PriorityLevel`, work estimator |\n\n### The `GenericAPIServer` and `Config`\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go` contains the `GenericAPIServer` struct: the central runtime object. It owns the `APIServerHandler` (the full HTTP handler tree), discovery endpoint managers, health check registries, the audit backend, and the `delegationTarget` pointer for the server chain.\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go` holds the `Config` struct, populated from option structs and then \"completed\" before constructing the server. Default values are set in `NewConfig`:\n\n```go\n// config.go:427-478\nreturn &Config{\n    BuildHandlerChainFunc:       DefaultBuildHandlerChain,\n    MaxRequestsInFlight:         400,\n    MaxMutatingRequestsInFlight: 200,\n    RequestTimeout:              time.Duration(60) * time.Second,\n    JSONPatchMaxCopyBytes:       int64(3 * 1024 * 1024),\n    MaxRequestBodyBytes:         int64(3 * 1024 * 1024),\n    ...\n}\n```\n\nThe field `BuildHandlerChainFunc` is the primary extension point for the filter pipeline\u2014it defaults to `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` but callers may replace it entirely.\n\n### `APIGroupInfo` and REST Storage Registration\n\nAn API group is attached to the server by constructing an `APIGroupInfo` and calling `InstallAPIGroups`:\n\n```go\n// genericapiserver.go:71-98\ntype APIGroupInfo struct {\n    PrioritizedVersions          []schema.GroupVersion\n    VersionedResourcesStorageMap map[string]map[string]rest.Storage\n    Scheme                       *runtime.Scheme\n    NegotiatedSerializer         runtime.NegotiatedSerializer\n    ParameterCodec               runtime.ParameterCodec\n    ...\n}\n```\n\nThe `VersionedResourcesStorageMap` maps `version \u2192 resource-name \u2192 rest.Storage`. `InstallAPIGroups` (`genericapiserver.go:876`) iterates the versions, calls `installAPIResources`, and registers discovery handlers. `InstallLegacyAPIGroup` does the same for the `/api` (core) prefix.\n\n### The `Store` \u2014 Generic CRUD Engine\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go` contains the `Store` struct, which is the standard CRUD/Watch implementation. Every built-in resource embeds a `Store`. It delegates to a `DryRunnableStorage` (wrapping `storage.Interface`) and enforces business logic through strategy objects:\n\n```go\n// store.go:100-248 (selected fields)\ntype Store struct {\n    CreateStrategy rest.RESTCreateStrategy\n    UpdateStrategy rest.RESTUpdateStrategy\n    DeleteStrategy rest.RESTDeleteStrategy\n    BeginCreate    BeginCreateFunc   // optional \"transaction\" hook\n    AfterCreate    AfterCreateFunc   // optional post-create hook\n    BeginUpdate    BeginUpdateFunc\n    AfterUpdate    AfterUpdateFunc\n    AfterDelete    AfterDeleteFunc\n    Decorator      func(runtime.Object) // exit hook after every storage read\n    Storage        DryRunnableStorage\n    ...\n}\n```\n\nStrategies carry the actual business logic (field immutability, name generation, namespace defaulting, validation). The `Store` itself is storage-agnostic; it invokes the strategy before writing and after reading.\n\n### The `APIServerHandler` \u2014 Routing Architecture\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/handler.go` describes the dual-routing system:\n\n```\nFullHandlerChain \u2192 Director \u2192 GoRestfulContainer (API paths)\n                            \u2192 NonGoRestfulMux    (utility paths: /healthz, /metrics, /openapi)\n```\n\n`GoRestfulContainer` (from `github.com/emicklei/go-restful`) handles structured REST API routing with content negotiation. `NonGoRestfulMux` is a simple `PathRecorderMux` for everything else. The `Director` inspects the incoming path to decide which branch to use.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n\nThis section traces a `kubectl create deployment` (`POST /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/default/deployments`) through the full stack.\n\n### Phase 1: Outer Filter Chain (`DefaultBuildHandlerChain`)\n\nThe filter chain is assembled inside-out: each `handler = WithX(handler, ...)` call wraps the existing handler in a new outer layer. The code in `config.go:1015-1096` shows the exact wrap order. When a request arrives, it traverses these filters from outermost to innermost:\n\n1. **`WithAuditInit`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/audit_init.go`) \u2014 allocates an audit event for the request.\n2. **`WithPanicRecovery`** (`pkg/server/filters/wrap.go`) \u2014 catches panics, converts them to 500s.\n3. **`WithMuxAndDiscoveryComplete`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/mux_discovery_complete.go`) \u2014 blocks requests until all API paths are installed (prevents spurious 404s at startup).\n4. **`WithRequestReceivedTimestamp`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/request_received_time.go`) \u2014 stamps the request receipt time into the context.\n5. **`WithRequestInfo`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go`) \u2014 parses the URL into a `RequestInfo` struct (verb, resource, namespace, name) and injects it into the context.\n6. **`WithRoutine`** (optional, feature-gated) \u2014 executes downstream handlers in a new goroutine to minimize stack depth.\n7. **`WithLatencyTrackers`** / **`WithHTTPLogging`** (`pkg/server/filters/`) \u2014 per-filter latency metrics and structured logging.\n8. **`WithRetryAfter`** (optional) \u2014 rejects new requests with HTTP 429 during graceful shutdown, adding `Retry-After: 1` and `Connection: close` headers.\n9. **`WithHSTS`** / **`WithCacheControl`** \u2014 response header policies.\n10. **`WithProbabilisticGoaway`** (optional) \u2014 probabilistically sends `GOAWAY` on HTTP/2 connections to trigger client reconnection and load rebalancing.\n11. **`WithWatchTerminationDuringShutdown`** / **`WithWaitGroup`** (`pkg/server/filters/waitgroup.go`) \u2014 tracks in-flight requests for graceful drain.\n12. **`WithRequestDeadline`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/request_deadline.go`) \u2014 applies the request timeout from `Config.RequestTimeout` (default 60s) to the context.\n13. **`WithTimeoutForNonLongRunningRequests`** (`pkg/server/filters/timeout.go`) \u2014 enforces the deadline by running downstream in a goroutine and returning a timeout response if the deadline is exceeded. Watch requests bypass this.\n14. **`WithWarningRecorder`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/warning.go`) \u2014 thread-safe buffer for adding warning headers to the response.\n15. **`WithAuthentication`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go`) \u2014 runs the authenticator chain; on failure, invokes the `failedHandler` which returns `401 Unauthorized`.\n16. **`WithTracing`** (optional, feature-gated) \u2014 starts an OpenTelemetry span; placed _after_ authn so clients can influence sampling rates.\n17. **`WithAudit`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go`) \u2014 populates the audit event with user identity and response status.\n18. **`WithImpersonation`** / **`WithConstrainedImpersonation`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/impersonation/`) \u2014 checks and applies user impersonation (`Impersonate-*` headers), re-running authorization with the impersonated identity.\n19. **`WithPriorityAndFairness`** or **`WithMaxInFlightLimit`** (`pkg/server/filters/priority-and-fairness.go` / `maxinflight.go`) \u2014 either APF-based flow control (classifies request into a `FlowSchema`/`PriorityLevel` queue) or the simpler fixed limit.\n20. **`WithAuthorization`** (`pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go`) \u2014 invokes the authorizer chain; returns `403 Forbidden` on denial.\n\nAt this point the request is authenticated, authorized, and admitted through flow control. The body has still **not** been deserialized.\n\n### Phase 2: REST Endpoint Handler (`pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go`)\n\nThe `APIInstaller` (`pkg/endpoints/installer.go`) registered an HTTP handler for `POST /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/deployments` when `InstallAPIGroups` was called. That handler is `createHandler` in `pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go`:\n\n1. **Content negotiation** \u2014 selects input and output serializer based on `Content-Type` / `Accept` headers (`negotiation.NegotiateInputSerializer`).\n2. **Body read** \u2014 `limitedReadBodyWithRecordMetric` reads up to `MaxRequestBodyBytes` (3 MiB default), recording the byte count as a metric.\n3. **Decode** \u2014 `scope.Serializer.DecoderToVersion(decodeSerializer, scope.HubGroupVersion)` converts the wire JSON/YAML/protobuf bytes into the _internal_ version of the object via the `Scheme`'s hub-and-spoke conversion graph.\n4. **Field validation** \u2014 if `FieldValidation=Warn` or `Strict`, a strict decoder detects and surfaces unknown fields.\n5. **Admission (mutation phase)** \u2014 `admission.NewAttributesRecord(obj, ...)` constructs the `Attributes` interface. The field manager (`FieldManager.UpdateNoErrors`) sets `managedFields`. The `requestFunc` wraps the final storage call and is passed to the admission chain so plugins can introspect the storage outcome.\n6. **`finisher.FinishRequest`** \u2014 runs the actual storage call and admission inside a dedicated goroutine with the request context deadline.\n7. **Admission (validation phase)** \u2014 `ManagedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController` validates field manager annotations; then the generic admission chain's `Validate` pass runs across all validating plugins.\n8. **Storage write** \u2014 `r.Create(ctx, name, obj, validateFunc, options)` calls `Store.Create`, which invokes `CreateStrategy.PrepareForCreate`, `CreateStrategy.Validate`, then `Storage.Create` to write to etcd.\n9. **Response** \u2014 the stored object is serialized to the negotiated output format and written to `http.ResponseWriter`.\n\n### Phase 3: Storage Layer\n\nThe storage call descends through:\n\n```\nStore.Storage (DryRunnableStorage)\n  \u2192 cacher.Cacher  (implements storage.Interface)\n      \u2192 etcd3.store  (implements storage.Interface)\n          \u2192 etcd gRPC client\n```\n\nFor **writes**, the cacher delegates directly to the etcd3 store. For **reads and watches**, the cacher serves from its in-memory `watchCache` where possible, falling back to etcd on a cache miss.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Watch Cache Architecture\n\nThe watch cache (`pkg/storage/cacher/`) is fundamental to Kubernetes scalability. Without it, every controller's `WATCH` call would hit etcd directly, creating an unbounded fan-out.\n\n### Structure\n\n- **`Cacher`** (`cacher.go:262`) \u2014 the top-level struct; implements `storage.Interface` and acts as a transparent proxy, intercepting `Watch` and `List` calls.\n- **`watchCache`** (`watch_cache.go`) \u2014 an ordered ring buffer of recent `watchCacheEvent`s, plus a snapshot store of all current objects used for list serving.\n- **`cacheWatcher`** (`cache_watcher.go`) \u2014 one instance per active client watch; receives events from the `Cacher`'s dispatch loop and filters them against the client's label/field selectors.\n- **`indexedWatchers`** (`cacher.go:142`) \u2014 a map that routes incoming events to exactly the set of watchers that need them, using field-indexed lookup to avoid scanning all watchers for every event.\n\n### Initialization Sequence\n\n1. At startup the `Cacher` performs a full `LIST` of its resource from etcd to populate the `watchCache` snapshot.\n2. It records the `resourceVersion` from the list response.\n3. It starts a background `WATCH` from that version, feeding events into the `incoming` channel (`cacher.go:268`).\n4. A dispatch goroutine reads from `incoming`, updates the ring buffer, and fans out to all registered `cacheWatcher` instances.\n5. The `ready` gate (`cacher.go:280`) blocks any client `List` or `Watch` until initialization is complete.\n\n### Bookmark Events\n\nThe cacher sends `BOOKMARK` events to each `cacheWatcher` to keep the `resourceVersion` current even when no mutations are occurring. This prevents clients from drifting to a stale version that would require a full re-LIST from etcd on reconnect. Bookmarks are scheduled via `watcherBookmarkTimeBuckets` (`cacher.go:198`), with a default frequency of 1 minute (`defaultBookmarkFrequency = time.Minute`).\n\n### Consistent Reads from Cache\n\nFor consistent reads, the cacher first fetches the current `mod_revision` from etcd (a cheap point-read), then waits for its cache to be at least that version before serving. This avoids stale reads without requiring a full etcd round-trip for data.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Server Composition: The Delegation Chain\n\nThe `kube-apiserver` binary composes three `GenericAPIServer` instances into a delegation chain. The `DelegationTarget` interface (`genericapiserver.go:306-337`) defines how one server hands off to the next:\n\n```\nAggregator Server\n    \u2193 (delegate)\nKube API Server (core)\n    \u2193 (delegate)\nAPI Extensions Server (CRDs)\n    \u2193 (delegate)\nemptyDelegate (returns 404)\n```\n\nEach server's `Handler.Director` checks its own registered routes. On a miss, `UnprotectedHandler()` returns the delegate server's `Director` as the fallback handler (`genericapiserver.go:339`). This gives the aggregation layer first pick for extension API service paths, core APIs are handled next, and CRDs last.\n\nWhen an incoming request arrives for `/apis/mycompany.com/v1/myresources`, the Aggregator checks whether an `APIService` has claimed that path. If so, it proxies the request to the backing service's IP. If not, the request falls through the delegation chain. This composition is wired in `cmd/kube-apiserver/app/server.go`'s `CreateServerChain`.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Admission Control\n\nAdmission control lives in `pkg/admission/`. The key interfaces (`interfaces.go:122-173`) are:\n\n```go\ntype MutationInterface interface {\n    Interface\n    Admit(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) error\n}\n\ntype ValidationInterface interface {\n    Interface\n    Validate(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) error\n}\n```\n\nThe `chainAdmissionHandler` (`chain.go:23`) iterates registered plugins in order. The `Admit` (mutation) pass runs first across all mutating plugins, then the `Validate` pass runs across all validating plugins. Each plugin declares which operations it handles via `Handles(operation Operation) bool`:\n\n```go\n// chain.go:31-43\nfunc (admissionHandler chainAdmissionHandler) Admit(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) error {\n    for _, handler := range admissionHandler {\n        if !handler.Handles(a.GetOperation()) { continue }\n        if mutator, ok := handler.(MutationInterface); ok {\n            if err := mutator.Admit(ctx, a, o); err != nil { return err }\n        }\n    }\n    return nil\n}\n```\n\n### Admission Attributes\n\n`Attributes` (`interfaces.go:31-77`) is the interface passed to every plugin. It provides the decoded in-memory object, the old object (for updates/deletes), the GVK, user info, dry-run status, and a mutable annotation map written to the audit log. Critically, `GetObject()` returns the already-decoded object \u2014 admission is the first stage where the body is materialized as a Go struct.\n\n### Reinvocation\n\nThe admission chain supports reinvocation: if a mutating plugin calls `ShouldReinvoke()` on the `ReinvocationContext`, the entire mutation chain re-runs. This handles the case where plugin B depends on a field state set by plugin A's mutation.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Authentication and Authorization\n\n### Authentication (`pkg/authentication/`)\n\nThe authenticator chain is a union of configured authenticators (`request/union/`). The first authenticator to return a non-nil `user.Info` wins. Common implementations include:\n- `x509` \u2014 client certificate validation against a CA bundle\n- `bearertoken` \u2014 validates a token string (delegates to a `TokenAuthenticator`)\n- OIDC \u2014 validates JWTs from an external provider\n- Service account tokens \u2014 issued by the apiserver's own OIDC-like endpoint\n\nThe authenticator is wired into the filter chain at `config.go:1056`:\n```go\nhandler = genericapifilters.WithAuthentication(\n    handler, c.Authentication.Authenticator, failedHandler, c.Authentication.APIAudiences, ...)\n```\n\n### Authorization (`pkg/authorization/`)\n\nThe authorizer chain uses a union-or-default model with three possible responses per authorizer: `Allow`, `Deny`, or `NoOpinion`. `NoOpinion` passes the request to the next authorizer. `Deny` short-circuits immediately. If all authorizers return `NoOpinion`, the request is denied.\n\n---\n\n## 8. API Priority and Fairness (APF)\n\nWhen `FlowControl` is configured (the default since 1.20+), `WithPriorityAndFairness` (`pkg/server/filters/priority-and-fairness.go`) replaces the simpler `WithMaxInFlightLimit`. APF:\n\n1. Classifies the request into a `FlowSchema` using the subject (user/group/service account) and resource type.\n2. Assigns the request to a `PriorityLevel` queue.\n3. Estimates the request's \"work\" (`flowcontrolrequest.WorkEstimator`) using the resource type and object count from `StorageObjectCountTracker.Get`.\n4. Queues the request if concurrency is saturated, or rejects with HTTP 429 if the queue length limit is exceeded.\n\nThe default fallback (`WithMaxInFlightLimit`) applies fixed limits of 400 read and 200 mutating concurrent requests (`config.go:443-444`).\n\n---\n\n## 9. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 9.1 `BuildHandlerChainFunc` \u2014 Filter Pipeline Replacement\n\n```go\n// config.go:429\nBuildHandlerChainFunc: DefaultBuildHandlerChain,\n```\n\nReplacing this function allows embedding servers to add custom middleware globally or to disable specific standard filters. The function signature is `func(http.Handler, *Config) http.Handler`. **Risk**: omitting a standard filter (e.g., authorization) creates security holes. Filters that panic or block make the server unresponsive.\n\n### 9.2 `PostStartHooks` and `PreShutdownHooks`\n\n```go\n// hooks.go:43-46\ntype PostStartHookFunc func(context PostStartHookContext) error\ntype PreShutdownHookFunc func() error\n```\n\nAdded via `Config.AddPostStartHook`. These run asynchronously in separate goroutines after the server starts listening. They receive a `PostStartHookContext` with a `LoopbackClientConfig` for authenticated self-calls. **Risk**: a hook that never completes consumes a goroutine indefinitely; hooks that conflict (e.g., two hooks writing the same Lease) must implement their own coordination.\n\n### 9.3 Health and Readiness Checks\n\n```go\n// config.go:570-580\nfunc (c *Config) AddHealthChecks(healthChecks ...healthz.HealthChecker)\nfunc (c *Config) AddReadyzChecks(healthChecks ...healthz.HealthChecker)\n```\n\n`healthz.HealthChecker` exposes `Name() string` and `Check(*http.Request) error`. Extension servers add checks for custom dependencies. A failing readiness check prevents load balancer traffic without killing the process. The `StorageReadinessHook` is registered automatically by `InstallAPIGroups` for all backing storages.\n\n### 9.4 REST Storage Interfaces \u2014 Capability Discovery\n\n`pkg/registry/rest/rest.go` defines a rich set of optional interfaces. The `APIInstaller` discovers capabilities at install time via type assertions:\n\n| Interface | Enables |\n|---|---|\n| `rest.Getter` | `GET /resource/{name}` |\n| `rest.Lister` | `GET /resource` |\n| `rest.Creater` | `POST /resource` |\n| `rest.Updater` | `PUT /resource/{name}` |\n| `rest.GracefulDeleter` | `DELETE /resource/{name}` with grace period |\n| `rest.Watcher` | `GET /resource?watch=true` |\n| `rest.Patcher` | `PATCH /resource/{name}` |\n| `rest.TableConvertor` | Tabular output for `kubectl get` |\n| `rest.StorageVersioner` | Storage version migration support |\n\nImplementing only the interfaces you need keeps the API surface minimal and avoids registering unsupported HTTP verbs.\n\n### 9.5 `Store` Hook Functions\n\nThe `Store` struct exposes lifecycle hooks called at specific points in the CRUD path:\n\n| Hook | Type | Called when |\n|---|---|---|\n| `BeginCreate` | `BeginCreateFunc` | Before persistence; returns a commit/rollback func |\n| `AfterCreate` | `AfterCreateFunc` | After successful persistence, before `Decorator` |\n| `BeginUpdate` | `BeginUpdateFunc` | Before persistence |\n| `AfterUpdate` | `AfterUpdateFunc` | After successful persistence |\n| `AfterDelete` | `AfterDeleteFunc` | After deletion |\n| `Decorator` | `func(runtime.Object)` | After every read from storage |\n| `ShouldDeleteDuringUpdate` | `func(ctx, key, obj, existing) bool` | Whether an update should become a delete |\n\n**Risk**: the `Decorator` runs on every read including list and watch results. As documented in `store.go:164`, it \"_cannot be watched_\" and is \"_intended for integrations that are above storage_.\" Heavy computation here directly dominates list latency under load.\n\n### 9.6 Admission Plugins\n\nAdding an admission plugin requires:\n1. Implementing `MutationInterface` and/or `ValidationInterface`.\n2. Registering it with the plugin registry (`admission/plugins.go`).\n3. Providing a `PluginInitializer` (`admission/interfaces.go:159`) if the plugin needs shared resources (informers, clients).\n\n`RecommendedOptions.ExtraAdmissionInitializers` (`options/recommended.go:47`) provides the hook for extension API servers to inject their own initializers without touching the plugin registry.\n\n### 9.7 `RecommendedOptions` \u2014 Extension API Server Bootstrap\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/recommended.go` packages the most common configuration needs:\n\n```go\ntype RecommendedOptions struct {\n    Etcd           *EtcdOptions\n    SecureServing  *SecureServingOptionsWithLoopback\n    Authentication *DelegatingAuthenticationOptions\n    Authorization  *DelegatingAuthorizationOptions\n    Audit          *AuditOptions\n    Features       *FeatureOptions\n    CoreAPI        *CoreAPIOptions\n    Admission      *AdmissionOptions\n    EgressSelector *EgressSelectorOptions\n    Traces         *TracingOptions\n}\n```\n\n`DelegatingAuthenticationOptions` and `DelegatingAuthorizationOptions` configure the server to delegate authn/authz decisions to the main `kube-apiserver` (via `TokenReview` and `SubjectAccessReview` APIs), which is the recommended pattern for extension servers. Calling `RecommendedOptions.ApplyTo(config)` applies all of these in the correct dependency order.\n\n---\n\n## 10. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 10.1 etcd as the Single Source of Truth\n\nAll writes go through etcd. If etcd is unavailable:\n- Mutating requests fail immediately: the etcd client returns an error; `Store.Create/Update/Delete` propagates a 500 or 503.\n- Read requests _may_ still be served from the watch cache for `ResourceVersion=\"\"` (best-effort) reads. Consistent reads stall because the cacher cannot confirm freshness.\n- A prolonged etcd outage causes the watch cache to stall; the `ready` gate flips to `false` until the background watch reconnects and the cache catches up.\n\n### 10.2 Watch Cache Memory Pressure\n\nThe `watchCache` ring buffer retains events for `DefaultEventFreshDuration` (75 seconds by default, `cacher.go:72`). Each `cacheWatcher` has an input buffer channel; if a slow client cannot drain events fast enough, the `cacheWatcher` forcibly terminates the watch (forcing a client re-LIST). In large clusters with many resources and many controllers, the aggregate memory for all watch caches can reach multiple gigabytes.\n\n### 10.3 Request Body Size Limits\n\nThe default `MaxRequestBodyBytes` is 3 MiB (`config.go:466`), matching the etcd recommended maximum. JSON payloads are larger than their proto equivalents; the comment in config explains the 2\u00d7 factor for JSON-to-proto growth during write. Exceeding the limit returns HTTP 413. The related `JSONPatchMaxCopyBytes` limit (also 3 MiB) bounds the total data movement in a JSON Merge Patch.\n\n### 10.4 Optimistic Concurrency\n\nEvery object's `resourceVersion` maps to etcd's `mod_revision`. Updates must supply the current `resourceVersion`; a mismatch returns HTTP 409 Conflict. This is implemented in `storage/etcd3/store.go` using etcd's compare-and-swap transaction. Clients must implement retry logic; the standard `client-go`'s `RetryOnConflict` helper addresses this.\n\n### 10.5 Handler Chain Construction Ordering\n\n`DefaultBuildHandlerChain` wraps handlers inside-out, so the last `handler = ...` line in the function (`WithAuditInit`) executes first at request time. This ordering is load-bearing: tracing is placed _after_ authentication specifically to allow authenticated clients to influence sampling rates. Placing a filter in the wrong position (e.g., authorization before `WithRequestInfo` populates the context) would cause nil-pointer panics or incorrect behavior.\n\n### 10.6 Graceful Shutdown Sequencing\n\n`lifecycle_signals.go` documents the shutdown protocol precisely:\n\n```\nT0:        SIGTERM received \u2192 ShutdownInitiated \u2192 /readyz returns red\n                              \u2192 PreShutdownHooks run\nT0+70s:    AfterShutdownDelayDuration:\n           \u2192 HTTP server stops accepting new connections\n           \u2192 Active long-running requests receive GOAWAY\nT0+130s:   InFlightRequestsDrained (up to 60s ShutdownTimeout)\n           \u2192 audit backend flushed \u2192 process exits\n```\n\nThe 70-second default `ShutdownDelayDuration` exists to allow load balancer health checks to propagate before connections are dropped. During this window the server continues to serve requests normally. When `ShutdownSendRetryAfter=true`, the server instead continues listening but replies to new requests with HTTP 429 + `Retry-After: 1`.\n\n---\n\n## 11. Operational Implications\n\n### Performance\n\n**Serialization is the dominant CPU cost** for high-QPS read paths. The library stores proto encoding in etcd (via `StorageVersioner`) and serves JSON/proto/CBOR over HTTP. Content-type negotiation happens per request; `Accept: application/vnd.kubernetes.protobuf` reduces serialization overhead significantly for high-volume clients such as controllers.\n\n**The `Decorator` hook runs on every read**. A `Decorator` that allocates or performs I/O per object will dominate list latency for large collections. As noted in `store.go:164`, it is intentionally limited to data that \"_cannot be watched_.\"\n\n**Admission adds latency proportional to webhook round-trips**. Each webhook call is a synchronous HTTP POST. A webhook with P99 latency of 100ms on a frequently mutated resource (e.g., pods) adds 100ms to every create/update. Webhook timeout and failure policy must be configured deliberately.\n\n### Reliability\n\n**Webhook `failurePolicy` is a sharp edge**. `failurePolicy: Fail` (the default for most built-in webhooks) means a webhook that consistently times out blocks all writes to the targeted resource. `failurePolicy: Ignore` avoids the block at the cost of missing enforcement when the webhook is down.\n\n**APF misconfiguration can cause cascading failures**. An overly restrictive `PriorityLevel` that starves `system` or `leader-election` priority classes can prevent the cluster from recovering from failures. APF configuration is itself stored in etcd, creating a potential bootstrap deadlock if the server cannot read its own flow control config on startup.\n\n**The `StorageReadinessHook`** blocks `/readyz` until all registered storages report ready. Extension servers that register storage via `InstallAPIGroups` get this check automatically, which prevents traffic from being sent to the server before it has a coherent view of etcd.\n\n### Maintainability\n\n**Code-generation reduces drift**. `deepcopy-gen`, `conversion-gen`, and `defaulter-gen` produce the boilerplate needed by the `Scheme`. Running generators on every type change is critical; skipping them causes runtime panics (nil pointer in `DeepCopy`) or silent data loss (missing conversion paths between versions).\n\n**`RecommendedOptions.ApplyTo` is the correct entry point** for extension servers. It applies sensible defaults and wires delegating authn/authz automatically. Using raw `Config` directly risks omitting security-critical defaults.\n\n**The hub-and-spoke version model** means every new API version requires an explicit conversion to/from the internal hub version. Failing to provide a conversion function causes HTTP 406 Not Acceptable when a client requests an unhandled version, which is a silent API regression.\n\n---\n\n## 12. File and Directory Map\n\nThe following files are most important for understanding and extending the apiserver library:\n\n| File / Directory | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/ARCHITECTURE.md` | Official high-level architecture document with Mermaid diagrams |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go` | `Config` struct, `DefaultBuildHandlerChain`, server defaults |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go` | `GenericAPIServer`, `APIGroupInfo`, `InstallAPIGroups`, `DelegationTarget` |\n| `PreShutdownHookFunc` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/lifecycle_signals.go` | Shutdown sequence documentation and signal types |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/recommended.go` | `RecommendedOptions` for extension API server bootstrap |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/installer.go` | `APIInstaller` \u2014 maps REST storage to HTTP routes via type assertions |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go` | Full CREATE request lifecycle: decode, admission, storage write |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go` | Authentication filter |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go` | Authorization filter |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go` | URL \u2192 `RequestInfo` context injection |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/rest/rest.go` | All REST storage capability interfaces |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go` | `Store` CRUD+Watch engine, strategy hooks |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/interfaces.go` | `storage.Interface`, `Versioner`, `UpdateFunc` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/cacher.go` | `Cacher`, watch fan-out, bookmark scheduling |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/watch_cache.go` | Ring-buffer event store for the watch cache |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/etcd3/store.go` | etcd3 backend implementation |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/interfaces.go` | `MutationInterface`, `ValidationInterface`, `Attributes` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/chain.go` | `chainAdmissionHandler` iteration and reinvocation logic |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/filters/priority-and-fairness.go` | APF request dispatch |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/filters/maxinflight.go` | Simple in-flight limit fallback |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/filters/timeout.go` | Non-long-running request timeout enforcement |\n",

# Kubernetes API Server Library: Subsystem Architecture and Extension Guide

## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies

The `k8s.io/apiserver` library (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/`) is the reusable foundation upon which every Kubernetes API server is built. It is not the full `kube-apiserver` binary—it is the generic scaffolding that provides the HTTP serving infrastructure, request filtering pipeline, type-system integration, storage abstraction, and security plumbing. A consumer of this library instantiates a `GenericAPIServer`, attaches REST storage implementations behind `APIGroupInfo` descriptors, and gets a standards-compliant Kubernetes API surface for free.

### Upstream Dependencies

The library sits on top of:

- **`k8s.io/apimachinery`** — type system primitives (`runtime.Scheme`, `runtime.Object`, `GroupVersionKind`, codec infrastructure, field/label selectors)
- **`k8s.io/client-go`** — informers and the REST client used by the loopback client and optional webhook callers
- **etcd (via `go.etcd.io/etcd/client/v3`)** — the sole officially-supported storage backend, accessed through `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/etcd3/`
- **`k8s.io/kube-openapi`** — OpenAPI v2/v3 spec generation and serving

### Downstream Consumers

- **`kube-apiserver` core** (`pkg/controlplane/`) — registers built-in API groups by calling `GenericAPIServer.InstallLegacyAPIGroup` / `InstallAPIGroups`
- **`kube-aggregator`** — builds an aggregation-layer server on top of the library
- **`apiextensions-apiserver`** — uses the library to serve CRDs
- **Extension API servers** built with `apiserver-builder` or manually using `RecommendedOptions`

### Boundaries

The library handles everything between network bytes and your storage call: TLS termination, authentication
... (truncated)

# Kubernetes API Server Library: Subsystem Architecture and Extension Guide

## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies

The `k8s.io/apiserver` library (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/`) is the reusable foundation upon which every Kubernetes API server is built. It is not the full `kube-apiserver` binary—it is the generic scaffolding that provides the HTTP serving infrastructure, request filtering pipeline, type-system integration, storage abstraction, and security plumbing. A consumer of this library instantiates a `GenericAPIServer`, attaches REST storage implementations behind `APIGroupInfo` descriptors, and gets a standards-compliant Kubernetes API surface.

### Upstream Dependencies

The library sits on top of:

- **`k8s.io/apimachinery`** — type system primitives (`runtime.Scheme`, `runtime.Object`, `GroupVersionKind`, codec infrastructure, field/label selectors)
- **`k8s.io/client-go`** — informers and the REST client used by the loopback client and optional webhook callers
- **etcd (via `go.etcd.io/etcd/client/v3`)** — the sole officially-supported storage backend, accessed through `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/etcd3/`
- **`k8s.io/kube-openapi`** — OpenAPI v2/v3 spec generation and serving

### Downstream Consumers

- **`kube-apiserver` core** (`pkg/controlplane/`) — registers built-in API groups by calling `GenericAPIServer.InstallLegacyAPIGroup` / `InstallAPIGroups`
- **`kube-aggregator`** — builds the aggregation-layer server on top of the library
- **`apiextensions-apiserver`** — uses the library to serve CRDs
- **Extension API servers** built with `apiserver-builder` or manually using `RecommendedOptions`

### Boundaries

The library handles everything between network bytes and your storage call: TLS termination, authentication, author
